Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter or bathe as much as the limb is relaxed, and when he has entered or washed, the pain will go away and be healed
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And ointments that no one must use with such medicines, except after the evacuation of pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And it is said that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with a piece of charcoal, if it helps with moisture; it must be made in a moderate part.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb and the great toe and the other that is called the fossilemma
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking charcoal chips dry, and burning them until they are coals, and putting them on the linen, and letting them stay until they are stained; and do this again, and do not stop doing this until you think by sense that it has gone down to the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "charcoal cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from sitting or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things like cold spreading matter, of none of these signs is the cautery useful, for it is only for what comes from the infusion of cold matter
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be devoid of foul pills or other things, that one should make on his back, to the left or to the right where the pain persists, three lines marked with a needle, and in the center line three cauteries or more according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called the "pointed" cautery. And if you see, make two or three cauteries at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small child, and the signs of its approach are when it has twisted the skin around the joint when it happens, and fear; and you find behind the lower spine in the back and on the appearance that comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize with the fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns some part of the spine excessively.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	If you see that the cautery has burned two or three lines deep on the spine, and that the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, take care that you do not cause further damage to the nerve in haste.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when the pain originates in the heel, it is commonly called "podagre." When the cause is cold and the condition does not respond to medicines, it may be cured by cautery in a partial manner: make the mouth of the cautery enter the joint at the heel and use the cautery of olive oil in this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the bone, if you cauterize with the whole cautery, we call that a “point”.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is pain that comes up to the shoulder and other joints, and this happens many times, if you cauterize on each shoulder three cauteries or four on each part, with the whole olive cautery; and if you must do more, do so, but do not keep your hand firm for longer than necessary until the sensation of pain has passed
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are as far as the hands, if you prick at the base of the nail two lines; and if there remains no pain in that spot, if you prick above the wrist and below the thumb; and if the pains go down to the buttocks or down to the elbows, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient well and give medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him well-governed and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is fractured, and the bones descend as coions, this is new; so if you see that it must be cured, do not move it immediately; and use things that leave the belly exposed, so that the pain descends from the belly; then make it sit on its buttocks between your hands, and command it to hold its shoulder tight until the bones are repaired, and hold it at your sides, and mark an indentation on the scapula above the elbow, and do all that is similar to half of a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery thus:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is soft and he sweats sensationless.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the bowels from their place; and he holds your hand so that they do not return backwards; and do well the wounds of the patient, and put some sponges under his chest and two towels on his buttocks; and another on his hands; then put the cautery on the sign at all his hand, and his arm straight and firm until you have reached the bone; and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you have reached the bone; and beware carefully that the bowel does not protrude when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that by this means the patient does not die or anything worse
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And soaks that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it must be known that the burnings of small hairs must be subtle in measure according to the size of the person; after three days cure the limb of the burnings as long as the scab is bony; after cure other ointments until it is healed; and keep the patient lying down for forty days upon his back until the wound is well closed; and it must be known that their nourishings must be prolonged in length, so that the boils do not emerge when he is moved to his bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wishes to rise, let him be supported with a good bandage, and let him rest for forty days; and let him have good rest, that he works little and be careful of eating too much drink and eating too much food; and when he has done this teaching if he is completely healed
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall tell you afterwards the treatment of the tail in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the route of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When they come out through other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow any more, if you do the fire cautery three times as much as before; afterwards treat according to what we have said; neither of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized with the fire at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the limb and make a line over the belly of the wound, and another at the bottom, and hold your hand firmly over the entire cautery needle.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	There is no ancient pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, or to the hip or to wound, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medical treatment is not worth it, then it is recommended to cauterize with the cautery called "pins", and to cauterize according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its toughness and its swelling and its pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sound after the first cautery, it is well; if not, repeat the cautery upon this one, for it is customary that it must burn towards the member that is nearest, because it is certain that you will make the cauteries as long as the patient is sound.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from sitting or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not sufficient; therefore it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with the cautery in accordance with the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its toughness and its twisting and its pain. If it is cured with the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery again. Indeed, it is customary that it must be burned towards the adjacent limb, for it is believed that in this way one can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The disease does not yield to cautery at any time, and even the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see it cauterized? Take warning if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not desist or linger, for you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the whole sickness; then make five cauteries upon the head: one at the new bone, and the other towards the front at the end of the beard; two upon the two corners, and one behind upon the heel; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries are coming up to the bone, and as long as the scabs come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize upon the mouse according to what is before you.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	If mixed moisture is scattered everywhere; and it becomes apparent, if you command to cauterize from these cauteries which we have said or chief, namely cauterize once low down, and twice on the spine of the neck, three on the spine of the back, one great one on the armpit and one elsewhere, and twice on the two scapulae, twice on the flanks, twice on the tendons of the wrist and elbow, and once on any joint of the hands and feet, and on the sinuses of the hands; take care of the nerves which are on the back of the calcaneus, so that you do not burn them; and never make an incision on the bone of the eyebrow, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And so it is that the more the patient does cautery, the more aid he does himself, and must profit from it; and so it is that the patient does not feel any pain from the cautery as long as he feels it in his sound sense, for the flesh is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the cautery must be great and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the handling of things.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the wound several times with flour and honey and other cures until it is healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not well, then you must cauterize on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and whether the cautery should be deep or superficial in the thickness of the skin; then cure the wound with ointments until it is healed
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never do we cauterize at the wrist, elbow, or back, at the issue of a nerve that makes the limb immobile; for if it is ossified, it swells up; and in no way do we interfere with it unless we are skilled in bones and the issues of nerves that move in flesh.
de albaras	When swelling arises in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not completely healed, then it must be cauterized on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and either the cautery should be applied once in the middle of the swelling or several times at the edge. Then it must be dressed with ointment until it is healed. And under no circumstances should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the site of a nerve that makes the limb immobile. And if it is a bony swelling, all these things must be known about the limb and the course of the moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicines are of no avail, then it must be cauterized with a single burn, according to the amount of swelling in the area, until the swelling is hard and changes colour; then it must be dressed with flour from time to time, with rose oil and plantain leaves, with charcoal and alum, one part of each; and all these things must be mixed together, and bound with a bandage, and left in place until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil starts to form, and you see it stop growing, if you cauterize at the level of the circle that appears around it, all around the boil.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And indeed they say that we should cauterize at the middle of the boil; but in my opinion, that does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that it is better to leave it alone; and the right thing to do is to cauterize around the circumference, at the level called the "circle", as we have said before.</start_of_turn
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has an ailment which is called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or through excessive pain that the patient experiences while decrepit (that is to say when he is too old), and there is little blood, or by tension; and you see it haste to heal: then you must cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; then leave it be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that it is perishing throughout the entire cautery, if it is hot, make the cautery smaller; for this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries perceive the pain, and be such cauteries that the patient feels relief in parts as the process of decay advances.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then leave it be until it is perfectly healed
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another disease of this kind is called "corrodens," and is nothing other than a swelling of a limb, for it swells the limbs just as the fires swell the lines of dry things.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the limb that can endure fire cautery, then extinguish the cautery needles closely spaced, as much as it is convenient for the limb or the disease; after having cauterized all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains except for the bone itself.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it rest for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs a bandage soaked in oil until the cauterized parts are ossified, and all the corruption is gone
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of wounds caused by these embers.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days the hair has not grown back, it is well; and if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on what remains undecayed.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy has never been cured by any medicine except for the fire cautery; but every time the fire cautery is of greater aid, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	portions that come as pieces.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that when hairs grow back, a disease called “clos” appears according to our understanding, and is a great burdensome burden that causes great pain
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	If you are to cauterize with fire, let the hair grow as long as a pine cone; and make it of fine iron to the measure that it can penetrate the hair root thoroughly, and there must be small margins; after that, put all around the hair root, and press your hand firmly over the root until it comes to the front of the hair; and leave it in place for three days until it begins to emit pus; then make an ointment of bruised sage leaves with oil, and leave the ointment on all night, and close the wound tightly and it will be healed from its root.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the swelling by applying pressure until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if there are converted by boils, and often happen in hands and feet, if you must bring the burn closer, apply a lukewarm cautery; and this is part of the method: take a needle of spiderwort or iron, or a pine cone, and put on the hair and the hair root, that is to say, to prick the hair; and put the needle on so that it touches all around, then put a little bit of warm water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the margin of the needle comes to the root of the hair, and can find the warm water going deep just to the root; and offer the patient a little dose of the warm water an hour; then leave it like that, and it will discharge all at its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do another, until you have scraped away all that is on the bone, then cure the wounds that remain and discharge the carbuncles that have formed.
li cure dou trembler	it cures trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shiver from cold or from a quartan fever or from another, if you order them to undergo three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach just below the naval; if you leave them thus, they will stop shivering and the disease will be overcome.
des pustules puans	When some shiver from cold or from a quartan fever or from another, if you order them to undergo three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach just below the naval; if you leave them thus, they will stop shivering and the disease will be overcome.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes from wounds appear bones bathed in pus, or boils filled with pus, which come from corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is possible at the outset when they appear, do the cautery on each head of the boils: a subtle cautery with a sponge of myrtle, or with the tip grasped by the fire, or with long acacia roots, or the lenticular cautery.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should the cautery be begun when they appear, according to this method, but should be broken up by the purulence from which they come, and they will be healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.</start_of_turn
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	When the artery is cut, there are often great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a mournful thing to extend it.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens, if you are quick to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and hold it tight without being appeased by the blood, and does not bleed any more; then take again the olive cautery, large or small as you please, and when they are all red; then take hold of the thumb or great toe as much as is necessary so that the artery is not obstructed, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery until it is fixed.</start_of_turn
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out fiercely when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take hold of another cautery that is in the fire immediately.</start_of_turn
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do this one after the other until the limb is stretched out; keep guard that you do not touch the nerve which is below, and that no other mischief comes upon the patient; and take care that when the artery is large, it is not properly filled even with the best treatment, except in three ways: by cautery, or by extraction if it is not otherwise treated, or by strong stitching with thread, or by medicines placed on which have power to fill the blood.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about a rest of the limb by tightly draping it or by putting on hot things upon it, or other similar things, if this does not prove helpful in no way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no remedy and no medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it firm until it is healed from the wound and from the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it often with cold water so that it should be cold as long as the limb is frozen and swollen and healed; and do poultices in front of that which he must cauterize and medicate
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This sentence translates as:
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said in the first chapter that every disease in which it is appropriate to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, we shall consider the incisions, the causes, the instruments, and the forms of cautery; and in this chapter we shall treat the chief diseases from the head downwards, and I shall speak of them by the same way as before because we have found it to be lighter in this way.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, I must tell you, dear sir, that there is more danger and fear in this chapter than in all the previous cautery, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not be rash.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in many ways people come to harm in treating.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who are aware of their ailment but move carelessly because of their fear of the disease, and of the greatness of their malice; and of these we must have fear.</start_of_turn>
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of those who make you sense, saying: "Wait, I am ready"; and the disease is desperate.</start_of_turn
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	I tell you only that you must allow those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not fear me foolishly but prudently of what you are certain, and of what you have learned and practiced; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation is either accomplished or turned; and this will help you to achieve good renown, glory, and memory forever.</start_of_turn
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords, you must understand and be skilled, and if you turn to the inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier. dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded you this chapter by dividing into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have commanded from head to foot, because it will be easier for you to find what you have desired.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Saiches that this disease comes from time to time with great swelling of the head of the child; and when the swelling is too great, the head of the child is strained.  Never comes this from any other cause than that it is not set right.</start_of_turn>
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease leave so quickly as in the summer; and with all that I have heard, it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in parts rather than to cure it all at once.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in childhood when the shoulder was dislocated, the head grew so large that it could not be sustained; and it was believed that the moisture was so great that it became a tumor, and when this moisture is gathered between the bones above the scapula, between the humerus and the scapula, and the work is such that if the moisture is between the humerus and the scapula, and the incision is made too small, you must make a wide incision; and be as long as necessary, until the moisture has gone.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscess is larger, if you make two incisions like a cross, following this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture swells the bone, and you see the upper part of the forearm protruding beyond the lower part, and it is painful when you press it with your hand inwards, and it does not subside: if you suspect that the bone is fractured in two places, do this: make two incisions as I have said.
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out the moisture with all your might.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After you have drained the moisture, strip off the layers of cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave for five days; then remove it, and heal the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the head of the limb elevated, and give the patient dry meat in place of the moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.</start_of_turn>
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another method of incision is to look or open the opening of the abscess, and the collection of fluid; for it never stands before; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.</start_of_turn>
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor. de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the filling of the liquid, and you do according to what you can bear; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease which is called a "catarrh" of the eyes or the ear, and the disease is old, and the medical cure does not help, then the only remaining cure is to cauterize with the fire, since this will cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then, when you see them covered, that the patient raise his head; after that, rub the limb with a rough cloth until the veins open, then remove the patient’s collar from all the clothes; then look to see if the vein is open, and if the blood flows from one and from the other side as far as the ears, and if so, restore them; then tie the veins, and clamp one and the other with a sharp needle of two parts, until the size of the vein reaches the bone, and that is from the root of the chief.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see that, withdraw the sponge from the artery and tie it below, cutting as much as .ij. inches across the vein.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is tied, if blood spurts without stopping, continue to bleed upwards.</start_of_turn
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open on examination, if you deem it necessary, measure the amount of space of three fingers, then mark and hold it until the bone; what is to be done is to put six grains of salt in and, by chance, more or less, according to what the patient can tolerate, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point where the abscesses were, if the edges of the incisions do not meet, then strain the wound and bind it, and cure it until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open upon feeling, if it is thought that two fingerbreadths suffice, mark the spot and hold it firm until bone is reached; for what is to be done with blood that will be shed if more than two fingerbreadths are needed, or less, as the patient can bear, and the refilling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains over the bone point where the stitches were placed, if the wound edges do not meet, then strain the wound and tie it off, and cure it until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dropsy comes, and acute swelling, because of the moisture of tears and the choleric humours in the temples and the ancient saliva is lost, and similar things, and it is cured by means of medical treatments and all that does not help, if the arteries of the temples are extracted and cauterized, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And thus is the method of extracting them: if the patient causes the hair of his temples to recoil, he understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating; and is not closed as in some other people who are too cold. And if it is closed, he must tighten the patient’s collar with some cloth, then wipe the area with no rough cloth, and rise the area with warm water until the artery opens visibly; then take the sponge which is in this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then gently stretch the skin until you see the artery, then pull it up with tweezers, and withdraw it well from the tissues that are underneath; if the artery is taut, if the tendon has a bulge at the shoulder, then cut off that part according to the amount of the two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not fixed, if it leaps out without hesitation.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And thus is the method of extracting them: if the patient causes the hair of his temples to recoil, he understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating; and is not closed as in some other people who are too cold. And if it is closed, he must tighten the patient’s collar with some cloth, then wipe the area with no rough cloth, and rise the area with warm water until the artery opens visibly; then take the sponge which is in this form: then scratch the skin lightly until you see the artery, then pull it upwards with pincers, and take hold of the area with towels that are soaked with warmth. For if the artery is subtle, if its tip is at the root of the nail, then support that part according to the quantity of blood that is lost. For if it is not supported, it will burst without doubt.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is useful for finishing off moisture: because of this it is of greater aid in moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the fire cautery is useful for extracting arteries that are filled with much fat and putting on strong stitches; and when you remove them, if there is no cure for dry medicines that make new flesh grow, and strong stitches, until they are healed; and if you do not take care of the artery as much as you should, if you hurry to cover with cautery, or if you use vinegar in your hand that is not stained; and if you do not have this present, if you must remove the vein you must do so while it is still warm, and rise the cold water until it stops bleeding, and strain as much as you can; and what is more numb and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein for a third of its length, but the cautery should be well spaced to prevent it from staying too long.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch. Then, when you have marked the area with ink, let the loop of the instrument rest burning over until it reaches the bone, and press the skin in one inch of the loop. Let the loops be spaced between the joints because they are not soldered by this cautery in any way. This is the form of the fire cautery.
des larmes	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch. Then, when you have marked the area with ink, let the loop of the instrument rest burning over until it reaches the bone, and press the skin in one inch of the loop. Let the loops be spaced between the joints because they are not soldered by this cautery in any way. This is the form of the fire cautery.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from veins that are above the root of the head, and it does not help any medical cure what is being done, and you see the patient’s face swelling, and feeling or front limping as if with fear; and if there are tears and moisture when paper is placed under them, and the paper is stained and scorched by the heat of the tears, if there is any hope of this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	If it is not firmly secured, if it leaps out without hesitation. It was formerly called the "cure contuse"; and you must make the patient with this disease let the hair grow long enough to have either a front or a border, then make three incisions or borders equally according to the length of the front; and let one of the incisions be as long as two teeth, doing so swallowing down the throat as far as necessary, and the other two as wide as two ribs from under the paper; and hold the incision of the arteries that are as wide as two ribs from under the paper; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and if there is any wound, let the amount be three teeth passing through the joints; and provide a piece of sponge and a towel to absorb the blood, then bind the instrument tightly with two parts of cord which is the shape.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	of the incision which is from the temple to the second incision; and pull out all the marrow that is between the two incisions to all the tissue which is above the bone, then do the rest of the wound until the other second, and then take out this dressing.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and is very well cut on one side, and on the other side is soft, do not cut deeply, for that is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge of the scalpel towards the outer side of the shoulder at the joint, and hold the cutting edge towards the bone, and hold the handle until it reaches the middle fracture line.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the blood vessels that descend from the head as far as the incision is continuous until it reaches the middle fracture line, and then do the same in the middle fracture line until the other edge; then withdraw the blood equally, and express the wound for the blood taken; then put in the wound a piece of cotton wool, and put on wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and herbs, and keep that there are no afterbleeds; and after three days remove the sutures, and there must be great pain to the bone, then treat the wound with basic oil of rose, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	because of the return of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute catarrh is present, you see the pupils tense and small, and the vision blurred; and the paper burns. The hair grows, and where formerly there was no pain, there is now great pain; the patient sneezes. Thus the discharge from these accidents is greater than from many veins, and the medicine that is usually effective fails in this case.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to recline his face, then make a great incision from ear to ear, and another one wide here below.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And instruct the patient to recline his face, then make a great incision from ear to ear, and another one wide here below. Begin from the temple on the left side to the temple on the right side, and make the incision reach the bone; and hold your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move towards the cheek. When the bone is exposed, if there is blood, evacuate it with a sponge, and then drain between the two layers of the incision and put in cotton wool, and try to hold it in place; then cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and keep it clean. When it has healed, if necessary, rub the bone until it begins to grow, and then cure it with drying things that will cause it to harden.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding the ear swelling,
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that is seen in the ears is one of three things: grains, or pus, or stone or like iron; or seed, as in grapes, beans, peas; or a flowing substance as in wound and boils and like things.</start_of_turn>
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When he pricks in the earlobe or any other way that does not fit with the ear, do not believe in the ear, but put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the earlobe, if no purple oil or oil of poppy seed comes out, then mix in extraction; and let him spit out bezoars, and press on the nose when he spits out, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and extend the ear downwards.</start_of_turn>
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times blood comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, mix in extraction as fine needles, for this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	When it bursts out with these bites, it is good; if this does not happen, do an incision with a fine needle; and if it does not burst with this, take a piece of gut and put some cotton around it, and press on the swelling above the gut as much as it will go without causing harm, and bring out the swelling.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in a hurry to make the incision above the ear, and if there is spasm, do as follows: make the opening wide enough for the patient to regain consciousness; then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty or bony prominence; and make the incision as wide as a crescent moon, as long as you can reach the bone, then remove the bone according to your ability, and drain the pus immediately from your mouth; and the healing will be perfect.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If there are grains of sand or gravel and it is painful, administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, administer sponge with slippery substances according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	mix in incision of that grain.</start_of_turn>
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this until you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract as fine needles and with suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.</start_of_turn

If that does not work, take many pins according to the length of his must hold and lighten, and put them in the fire; and put the patient one or two holes in the ear, and take out from its parts, and burn from another side, and pierce with another pin on the pin which is in the ear; and do not stop doing this until the pain is gone, and when it is burst it will be burst through; and if you see, take an onion, and put one of the heads of the shoulder in the ear, and the other head grasp with fire as long as the pain is not gone; then make the other half of the pins as long as the pain is gone, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is of small size, as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great size, it can be felt, so you must perform an extraction of wisdom teeth; and this is the easiest thing to do in the ear.

And let the wound be broad and deep. And let the silver or gold be thoroughly loosened from the bottom to the top, with a few slight tears, and from above over the distiller; and press with a well-made instrument of gold for this purpose. de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding the ear swelling,
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a mark upon their ear; and the same thing happens as with wounds or a burst ear drum in the ear, for these bursts never happen without leaving a mark on the ear, if one does not see them; and never is there any trace of having had a burst.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	No child is born without a mark upon their ear; and the same thing happens as with wounds or a burst ear drum in the ear, for these bursts never happen without leaving a mark on the ear, if one does not see them; and never is there any trace of having had a burst.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it that it is seen and known before and behind all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the bursting is of a burst ear drum or a swelling of the ear, if you have subtle pinches, and hold it lightly, as long as that burst is entirely bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operations are embedded in the ear, take a sharp scraper of the finer kind and burnish a little at the fire, then put in or remove the earwax.</start_of_turn
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the swelling which the patient feels at the ear, prick slightly, and hold that you do not hurt the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a plug according to the size of the hole, and the moisture in the Egyptian manner.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do anything until the wound is healed; then take a sponge and soak it in rose-water, sprinkle with powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swelling, it is likely that you must remove the plug and apply another sponge soaked in oil of roses and beeswax until the swelling subsides.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If blood vessels swell, immerse a sponge and wring it out in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments that are useful for stopping blood flow which is causing the swelling.
de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	From the stack of papers comes this treatise which comes from the blood of the eyes when they are moist and dry, if you stretch them out with nails and pinches, and grasp the root with a spatula; then extract the glassy vitriol that is bruised.
