And if you do not take precautions, if you cauterize with a subtle lens and cauterize afterwards the incision is worth moving; and many times it is repeated, can no longer stay rooted at their root; and when they are cauterized by fire, if they are burnt those roots and do not return whole
de la gresle	From the grease.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come out of paper things which appear greasy in their form and hardness; and for this reason this disease is called "granule", and is an assembly of large moisture in the substance of the hair and nails; the work is as follows: take hold of the granule when it moves from one side to the other, and this is a light matter to know; then do the following: make the opening wide, then burn the hair slightly, then take hold with tweezers, and grasp.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not perceive with the eye to cover, if nothing is hurting the patient; and if the swelling is great, if the contents are bulky, and the cure as long as it is sound; and if it is small, do not use force, for the swelling will restore itself and cause harm
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulin descends into the ear towards the upper part, reverse the belly, and pull out the granulin with tweezers, pressing from one side and the other; and if the belly is stripped by the incision, this will grieve nothing; and when the granulin is pulled out, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the belly of that which causes harm until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the tears
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	The wax is enclosed in papers of parchment, and this happens more often in women than in men, and causes great pain at their eyes, and comes the discharge in the mornings, and they cannot bear the sunlight for this reason, for the tears hurry to their eyes; and for this reason they lie with their faces downwards, and sleep on, and their parchment papers are wet with their tears which swell and appear covered in wax which opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb towards your chest and feel the wax between the bones.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	If the patient puts their head in their right place; and then take one towel of linen, and make a loop resembling a circle according to the quantity of exinach from the armpits, and put it on; and press on the two sides, so that the exinach is assembled like the circle; then make half of the moisture at the tip of the knife cutting a wound not greater than the wound made to the vein; and make the skin taut as long as you see the exinach; and in many situations comes out exinach from the wound, according to the shape of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the bones at all a blunt piece of marrow between your arms to the side, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as it is sparse; and keep that you do not join in the wound, that you do not live until all the marrow is out, that you do not bruise it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it emerges not at the commencement of the wound, if you expand a little the wound slightly until it opens; then remove it as we have said, and moisten the edges with oil and water, and place over it, and strain of bending.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if in such houses where they bruise themselves and put on to corrupt the moisture which is remaining
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure as long as it is healthy
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to the vein being cut, if the cure of closing wounds is applied as soon as it is sane.
des poilz des papieres	paper hair
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hairs attached other than their natural state, and are enclosed, if they irritate the eyes, they cause various diseases like tears which are usually excessive and softening of papers and gum, as much as this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by water-based medicine as it is before or alongside fire cautery, or by incision and suture or by ligature, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s head in your left hand, and move the paper from your right hand; if it is converted, that is good; if not, if there is a splinter of any size through all the thread below; either cut off the margin of the paper or the hairs will be cut off; and take out one thread from below at all the paper, and move it to the top; then make on the lower part of the paper, below the hairs, below all the fat up to the big tear, and pull out one thread, and put under the paper a small piece of cotton and bandage, and sign on the paper a figure like a nutmeg, and it must be so that the figure is according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is devised to you.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If the vein is cut, and the closing of wounds is applied as soon as it is healed. If there is much bleeding from the wound, apply a pad to the area for two lines as you have marked, and from the great toe to the little toe; make an incision at the root of the hairs as thick as a barleycorn, then place the ointment in one of the two angles that you have marked, then cauterize; then reunite the two layers with a needle and thread of fine silk, and drain the blood from the two sockets to the surrounding area. If you do this, the bleeding will stop; otherwise, if there is no other remedy, leave the sutures and the thread for three days or four; then close the wound with dry and constricting materials, because the blood will clot at the bottom of the wound and reunite the tissues, but the suture will be useless (as the old people say), and this is dangerous; or if there is another method: if you mark the wound with a figure similar to the berry of a myrtle, as we have told, and there are three grains of barley that measure according to the shape that is shown.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold back what is above with small forces evenly according to the form which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	If you are unable to hold the teeth steady, and the matter is not equal, take an awl or pierce with a needle, and pass the thread through the figure; and pass another thread loosely large, and the second thread loosely small, and assemble between your two the threads equally; then hold your hand equally, and hold all the leather above where you have signed, as we have said; then assemble the two layers of the wound by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerate and similar soothing ointments. Never again shall the hair of the beard be converted: if you use what we have said concerning the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard hair and the surrounding area as we have said, then make three incisions by art, and three threads as long as the beard and expand in a circle; and take three hairs from three parts or hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other securely over what rests on the beard oil, and strain the three boils from the three parts forming; and leave it for a few days, and the skin that has been strained will swell and darken and become black, until it disappears by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has a great force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound has healed, and if the vessel has burst, and will not bleed again; and this is the form of the two veins that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is a thread of silk subtle; then assemble the bones and do not let one touch the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be equal; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not tie the knots; then put the patient's hand in its place; and let the sun go if the work is finished, for it is a subtle and minor work; then draw out the needle to the end of the chase at the root of the hair and make it pierce in the skin as much as you can until you take it out according to the nature of the hair; then pull out the hair until it is gone for a quarter or a third or a half or more; then pull out your hand until the vein flees to the end of the chase with the natural position of the hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase at the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from under and you see it through the sight of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread and close the oil and leave it closed for a quarter or two days, until the hair has returned to its place and the burden is gone.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the putrefaction of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the corruption comes in its oil, if there are two methods: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes from the wound, or from a burn or from cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	The way to work in this matter is that you make that suture, and dry the flesh, and put inside threads of linen, and keep it until it is healed; and do not do anything but use things that dry and restrain
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, if the disease returns worse than before; but there are things that are softening, such as fennel; and alum or salt and seeds of flax being boiled, and ointment of aquilon melted in no oil, and it covers a cloth, and cure of that
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal in a different form than it had before; for this work that we have said is not fierce except in addressing this disease, that it does not return in a different form than before.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the burn that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is of sudden onset and which truly is called "axacrati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and burns and things of that kind; and the way of working in this matter is if you take an awl, because it has two holes, and the handle in the flesh, and it makes split the left earlobe so that the vein bursts out into two parts of the flesh; then the flesh is raised from below to the top of the awl, and the handle has one large splatter.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb returns to its place according to what is convenient, that is good; if not, take an awl and put it into the cut, and twist the limb, and make two cuts or break two bones inside the limb; and if there are two cuts of two angles of the incision that you have made, or make an angle so that when they are put together, the limb looks like a letter that has not "I griesche"; then break that bone, according to the quantity of its cost and weight, of that which teaches the limb, then join the two broken parts with a thread of silk; then bind up that which we have said of the mollifying medicines and of the bands, until it is healed
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fracture or a sprain or a cautery, if you must make a full incision along the hairs of paper, as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons know best how to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him in more diverse circumstances.
dou soudement de la papiere	And if the disease comes from a fracture or a sprain or a cautery, if you must make a full incision along the hairs of paper, as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons know best how to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him in more diverse circumstances.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling has happened at home in a part like this that the paper beneath is solidified with oil, and cannot move or do its natural work, if you must drink the point of a scraper from the paper, and hold it up; and extend as little as possible, as long as you can tolerate what is airy in the swelling, which must not be too much and not too little, for the patient must not suffer too much from the swelling and must not burn the oil; and for your incision, which you should carefully drain, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all that is assembled should be healed, and do not make any more cuts in the oily water, and lift the water soft and clear, and some vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put on the oil wool loosely in abundance; and after that use oil of meadowsweet and other things soothing as long as it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the root of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nails of the oil are of two kinds: one is nervous and similar to hard pitch, and the other is not nervous but is similar to white moisture congealed. When one touches them with fire and boils them with oil, they do not burn; and both appear to swell towards the greater marrow, spreading throughout the whole eye and the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to make the incision is as follows: if the patient places his head in a healthy position, then he opens the eye; and the physician holds the eyelid with his hand, then he cuts the nail with small double-edged scissors, and stretches it downwards; then he takes a needle, and puts in one hair of a horse, or of a calf, or of a bull, and one strong thread; and he doubles the point of the needle a little and fixes it into the nail, and pierces it through with the needle, and ties the nail with a thread and stretches it downwards, and washes all around the nail the costae of the nail which surrounds the nail-root and the hair to the hair, and leaves the natural moisture or the tear, if there is no occasion for tears to come out usually; and in no case does the nail retract only by the incision, and by the thread, as we have said; then he washes away all the surrounding fat with the sponge. This is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the sponge does not touch the fatty tissue and breaks it, and that the needle does not pierce through; and after the incision pour oil into the wound a little bit of burnt salve, and give some lard, and leave it until the other side; then cure what has come to pass until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the thread cannot enter, many times it is cured of this semblance of a nail of medicine; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you cover the oil of the patient, and take the sponge lightly somewhat like this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And withdraw the nail gradually, and if you see that it has diminished somewhat and the flesh has pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil lard, make lard and red salve and burnt salve, and squeeze out the oil until the other side; then repeat the other work according to this same work, until it is entirely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders you, if like an incision, if necessary, hold the milk and cure the wound first until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	If there appears fat in the oil during the night, if it is fat that is soft and not thick, that is not fat; then distil in the red oil of poppyseed, which is made from litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the seed that grows on the plum tree.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The fire cautery instructs the patient to leave the hairs long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary to nourish the cure with a weak oil from the natural way; and in the work of fire; and do not burn your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from the work.
des voines des eulz	des voines des eulz
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The red veins are covered in oil, and endure the gaze of the surgeon and absorb the oil throughout the day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The surgeon must first look at the oil covering the veins, for if they are strong, it is certain that there is no other disease except the swelling; so the surgeon should order the patient to put his head in a safe place, then suspend the veins throughout their length as much as possible, and let the physician decide on the extent of the suspension: either subtle or severe according to this manner.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	Red veins covered with fat, endure the sight of an eye and make the fat swell all the days. The physician must first look at the eye to see if the fat is soft or hard; there is no other disease more violent than this; therefore, the physician must do this part carefully: instruct the patient to put his head in his hand, then suspend the veins throughout their length as he deems appropriate, and let the physician double the ligature as much as he deems necessary:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then suspend the veins throughout their length as he deems appropriate, and let the physician double the ligature as much as he deems necessary:
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect everything in that hour, make a poultice upon the oil of soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave it in place until the pain is relieved and is assured after the burn is complete; then resume in the same manner as before until it is healed; and this is the way of action.
de la fistule de l’oil	And if you are unable to collect everything in that hour, make a poultice upon the oil of soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave it in place until the pain is relieved and is assured after the burn is complete; then resume in the same manner as before until it is healed; and this is the way of action.

The mire so named "arissati" fistule: when you cure it with cautery and medicine with burning aqua as I have said before, and it is not completely healed, if there is anything remaining on the burn, then you must measure it out, and draw out all the moisture, until the bone is exposed.

When the limb is open all around and there is no risk of disturbing the nerve, no reduction, if you must, bind the patient; then draw the limb back, apply a bandage or dressing in a counterclockwise direction to absorb; then apply oil.i. linen made of acacia, aloe, incense and mastic, and strain the oil, and apply it on bandages and cloths; keep the cloths in place if you take cloths enough soft, and double layer in three, and then put one on top of the other as much as there is oil between the layers; then strain the oil through a coarse cloth forming, and restart the dressing in a clockwise direction to absorb; then hold the dressing and leave the oil strained for a while and night, and if the limb softens, if you must, remove the oil; then reset the limb after the swelling and nut, and if you see the oil returning, that is good; if not, continue the dressing and cloths and the limb and the dressing until it is healed.

When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset, and there are papers coming out like grains of resin, and it is expected to see; then if you see it covered, the work is like biting an awl into the root of the limb up to this point, then insert another awl or there is double thread of the limb; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl in place; then hold the double thread and bind a part of the limb around, and strain it well, then pull out the awl and put on oily lint liberally; and leave it until the thread is severed with the limb, and cure the oil of comforting things until the wound is healed; and in no case is the wound to be restricted by the limb bandage part of a circular bandage, until it is healed.

de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	The disease called "alcunnati" is not fierce but dull, which is assembled in oil, resembling descending ice; it is not truly ice. The way it appears in this chapter is that if you make the patient sit on a chair that appears and is straight, then take hold of the head with your two hands, and move it until you see the dullness coming down towards your eyes; then either bind it tightly or leave the light unrestrained and see the patient's condition as he alone will tell. If it does not descend spontaneously, give it the appearance of ice; and when it descends, it is not apparent as ice as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and place it upon the caruncle with the edge of the conjunctiva touching the caruncle and the crown, as long as the boil is in its place; and when it comes out, distillate into hot oily ointment mixed with honey, or into vinegar or fenugreek boiled with honey, then apply another remedy until it is healed.

It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, apply light from the sun, and bathe the eye with pure oil and tighten the mouth firmly; then put your left hand over the eye if the eye is towards the left, or your right hand if the eye is towards the right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is towards the left, the instrument which is called the almond, or in your left hand if the eye is towards the right; then place the point of the instrument below the crown by the thickness of a hair in that which there is plenty of oil at the lower part of the tear; then draw the instrument called the almond efficiently, and restore your hand until it pierces the oil, and feel that the almond comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almond be at the height of the measure of the space from the plumule up to the end of the pupil; and that is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the caruncle, then withdraw the instrument until the eye is level or the liquid is gone, and then express the eye after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels a sudden pain now, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his eye.

And pierce only the conjunctiva slightly, and do not go too deep, but make the limb limp, then put in place the dressing, as we have said; and at the end of the work appears to the patient the sleeping attendant lying on his back in the dark; and let him have gentle nourishment, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and bind as he commands until daybreak; then take him out of this house into the open air, and make him spit, and let him see nothing, and then put on the bandage once more until the seventh day; and do not attempt anything else in the course of the treatment or after the incision now, but make sure that you nourish him, for in that way the pain will subside gradually.

de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint on the neck.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. If nothing remains to hold it, if the wound has all its edges loose, if nothing remains to keep it; if it does not settle, or if it is proud, or if there is an abscess, or if there are sharp objects in it, or if it is malignant, then hasten and cauterize as much as possible until all the edges are bound and fixed; then drain or remove the pus easily and quickly, or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he does not work, and moisture comes up to his jaws, the saliva that he has is sane; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, there is pus coming from under the bone above, because the instruments do not come through to the root: therefore it is necessary that you give him a thread of linen a palm’s breadth, and hold his hands, and put between each thumb an inch or less; and put the patient’s chin on the thumb of his right hand, and pull until it comes through from the mouth; and many times do the children do this, and it is a light matter for one who has seen it done; then keep the thumb that comes from the mouth in one hand, and the thumb that comes from the mouth in the other hand, and join the one after the other while we hold as we who are holding.

Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Be it silver or gold, resembling an overblown lamp, if like a cord; if you see it, make a closed loop, and keep the instrument flat to purge the chief; and have one hand on the chief to hold it when pouring oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the head of the neck a disease which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes very great indeed, so that it is seen; and for this reason it is necessary that you should immediately take hold of the beginning and break the bone, then put out the fire or the burning medicine; and if you delay in taking hold of it when it is great, if you do not take hold of it firmly, of a pale color, of little sense: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a burnt abscess, for when you take hold of it once, there comes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of pale color, and you see that you can take hold of it completely, if you see the patient vomiting and taking hold in vain, cure the limb of dry things and restraints.</start_of_turn>
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do not leave the hairy growth for too long, but take out the hair at its root, wipe the blood, and moisten the hair with Egyptian balsam, and reinsert it as before; do this for three days or more, until the hair has eaten away everything that is left of the carbuncle; then put on or take off a cautery every other day until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them as well. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, from which we distil oils and medicines or nothing.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it be known that this thing has not happened to any other, if you see that the wound is fresh throughout its extent; then join the two layers to a staple, and cure until it is healed. If the layers are already detached from one side and the other, if you escort all the parts around until they bleed, then reunite the two layers to a staple, and strain, and sprinkle upon it dragon’s blood powder and incense; and put upon the powders a piece of packing of great or other packing that will adhere, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, then cure it of its own accord until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir. des apostemes des levres	from the armpits of the arms.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home in the hands, there are from the thumbs to the little finger, some that are like grains of wheat, smaller and greater; thus it is that you must break the nails, make incisions at the base of each nail, and grasp them with tweezers and press them into the flesh; then employ the lancet after the incision of the carbuncle, until it is not stained; and then remove it easily, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the heel of the jaw.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens on the gums that a tumor appears, which they formerly called "albules"; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the socket or the blood out; then put out the lancet or other astringent and desiccant powders; and if the tumor comes back after the incision, and happens often, if you grasp it a second time, cauterize it: if it does not come back after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Whenever they are joined at the head of the tooth, between the gums, teeth that are loose and rough; never are the teeth black and yellowed towards, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if it is thought that one should make the patient sit between the hands, and that his shoulders are relaxed, and open the jaws or the teeth will burst open, until nothing remains; and then one makes black and green, yellow and other stains, as long as they are softened; and if one has seen this at the first attempt, it is well done; if this is not the case, one must repeat the second and third time, until everything is recovered; and the teeth that have been mentioned above have various forms of stripes, according to what the master of the work shows, for the raisers of teeth which one must drive out have other forms than those which one must drive between the teeth; and these stripes and others are seen with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you stay close to it for a while, because it must not be left alone; for it is a high-quality matter, therefore we have no excuse for neglecting it
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to endure, if you wish to be certain that he will endure.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient complains of pain, and it must either be very great or completely absent; and make him groan with pain; and whatever does not depart with this pain while the mischief lasts, for we have already wished to make it leave those scoundrels; and when you are quite certain that he will endure, if you escort the limb into the wound at all points; put on strong support to ward off the swelling from all parts; then pull the limb forward or hold it firmly at the first joint and the second; until it is well flexed, then secure the ties well; and let the patient’s own pain be his guide between his thighs, and hold him firmly so that he does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, stretch the tooth outwards along the ridge; and if it does not yield, take no instruments and hold it loosely within the gum, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is perceived to have penetrated and is twisted, if it is necessary, cover it with gauze; if the tooth is fractured, hold it firmly in place; if the strain is done too roughly, it will break from the strain; it is necessary to keep the tooth moist over the gum with a scraper.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be careful not to break it, and leave some of the root intact, and return to the patient with the greatest pain of the first.</start_of_turn>
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be warned that you must not do as the ignorant fools do, who without haste and without caution break the limb countless times, and do not bring anything except what we have told you; but they bring countless times by the infection of this great disease from the roots that remain, or from the limb that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and oil; and if blood comes, as it often does, apply a little vitriol; if this does not suffice, cauterize it.</start_of_turn>
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of instruments, since they must remain silent at first, whether with long points and broad handles, must not double in number when you draw the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when drawing, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck at the shoulder, if you must take out the soaked cotton swab from the wound, do so with forceps or your fingers.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	While the limb is still stiff, because it holds the nails that are clipped off and appear like nails, make incisions just like with a lime, and that is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not yield to all these tensions, if you can, uncover the bark entirely around the root, and put the instrument which is called the «althali», which is to say a palanche, because of this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it breaks not, and the root comes out by this, that is good; if not, if you aid it with all your tools, because the shapes will come after.</start_of_turn>
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has just rain, because of this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Or other instruments which precede the teeth, and of this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Or else great and firm to hold the bone, that it does not slip, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, if the disease has all of these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear contrary to their natural position, and their form is deformed, even in women of childbearing age, if it is suspected that they are deeply embedded and cannot be extracted without damage, then extract them entirely; and if they are embedded with the tooth, grasp this instrument which has a similar shape to a small beak, and which is made of iron without a jagged edge.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	When the tooth persists too long in the gums and in the hands, for the duration of the tooth's hardness, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you use a file that has the same shape as the tooth
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	When the tooth persists too long in the gums and in the hands, for the duration of the tooth's hardness, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you use a file that has the same shape as the tooth. And it is just like filing nails; and while you are filing the tooth slightly, so that it does not move too much, if it blanches, the tongue will bleed excessively, so if you want to avoid this, file the sharp edges until they are even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loosened, by percussion or with pliers, and the patient cannot press on what is hurting him except that it bleeds, and you must cure it with restrictive medicines, which is of no use; if you must restrain it with a gold wire, for the silver wire turns green and rusts, but the gold does not move; and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth moving, if you take hold of the wire and double it between the two teeth in front, then put the teeth between the other teeth, if there is one or more of them, until you see them steadily up to the sound tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand steadily and cautiously, until it does not move; and let your tie be at the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the shoulder with two pins and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and keep it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it so tight as it can remain stable, and if it slips or the pin breaks, if it is strained by another pin; if it should remain and serve its purpose, and that is the form of a knot and the figure of the arrangement of two teeth in front, and two teeth behind, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make its shape like a tooth of ivory, and put it back in its place where the fault is, and strain it as we have said, and hold and use it for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is this ligament that comes from the tongue or nature itself that is born without causing pain; or by accident of a deep wound. The work is such that you must see the patient’s mouth and have his tongue in your hand, and then grasp the large nerve as long as the tongue is displaced from its abode; and if there is duration or no sensation, and that is a sign of wound, if it should join the bone and grasp the ligament; and keep that the opening be not too wide, for the artery that is from the tongue; and when you have done this, if you raise the pale and easy blood, or cold blood, then put the tongue back with a little thread; and hold the patient’s tongue firmly at night, so that it cannot be soothed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If blood comes from a wound, take out the glass vial broken; if it does not go away, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a black or brown or hard bubble, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a carbuncle; and if it is declining with moisture, if there is blood, if you touch the wound, and you make a splatter of blood, and deliver from a part and from another; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on broken glass until it is stained, then return to your work until you have finished everything; then lift the pale liquid and the like, and treat with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there comes from the throat thick blood which is called “godath,” and these are properly two almonds; and when you treat them, as we have said before, and they are not healed, take care: if it is an abscess of small size and with a reddish pus, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, even though there is discharge of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will remove it, or it will break by itself; and if it is white in color and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover, but first look to see if the abscess is calm and peaceful.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	When you wish to set the dislocation, make the patient sit in the sunlight, and let the arm hang naturally by his side. Close his mouth and grasp his hands between his arms, and press his tongue against the instrument, as is its form. Let it be of silver or gold as thin as needles.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	... and if you see the abscess, take the sponge and wipe it in the abscess, and push it down further than you think; and do not put anything of the towels on it, then close the instrument over the abscess, as it is with a spoon; and all the while the patient’s shoulders are bent, one place over the other, and are very sore, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with pincers, know that this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with pincers, know that this is the shape:
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman with an abscess that was in her throat, that is to say a small abscess; and she had such a tight grip on her throat that she could neither breathe through her nose nor drink or eat, and she died within a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had forced two grains out of the two holes of the nose
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then I had to take hold of her again, and I oiled one eye, then I forced her to vomit, and in vomiting she expelled a great portion of bile; then I repeated the process in the other hole of the nose, and I closed her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I put the oil into the abscesses, and cut out a part of it, and only a little blood escaped; and when I had stopped bleeding from the wound in her throat, she began to drink water and then wine, and she continued to spit out blood for a long time; and the abscesses kept growing bigger; so I grasped them and cauterized them in her throat: after that she spat without pain; and I left those parts behind, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb descends at the shoulder, and it is escaped and is long, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "shoulder".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure brings no benefit, and you see that the wound is appeased, and it is subtle, if you must cut; and that which is round and compact and is not long; and that is bloody or dark-brown or black, if you must avoid the incision of the wound.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to what I have said, from its colour and its length, you must make the patient sit in the sun, and stretch out the tongue with the instrument which we mentioned before; then insert the unguent into the limb, and draw out the wound, and press on it with two fingers as I have said concerning the incision of the two almonds.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And must not cover more than the superfluous which is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, if you grieve the voice and the word; and after the incision, use of what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure as long as it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you must know that you must use something to restrain the patient at the cautery of the painful side.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is acute and hot

Take camomile, rue, origanum, ivy, and chamomile, and assemble all or some of them in a pot. Put some oil in it and boil. The pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot is one instrument that should be fixed according to this method.
