Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure the whole thing, if it is not firmly secured, the head of the shoulder will be perceived [as loose]; and comes blackening and corruption in its head and root; if you can drive out everything that is black and corrupted, then lie upon the place of honey and flour which is made of the peel of pomegranate seeds and sometimes, cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood flows away, if you mix the lunar cautery in this fashion:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two situations: that is, at the outflow of blood and at corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and withdrawn, if you bite or conduct the hair a span of plum, and the patient urinates; and when the hair has fallen out at the root of the hair which has not been cut, or there is a wound or incision, if you can then burn away the hair with the instrument that chews, until the thread is loosened and the head of the hair is freed from all parts; and if it is necessary to divide this, if you can burn it with the spatula without causing any damage to the head of the hair and the root; then gently wipe between them, and put on a bandage of fine linen soaked in cold water, which does not loosen
de la circoncision	with circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own free will, and do it with care, if we are able to make the best work, and the lightest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision in their laws, because they did not use it in their customs, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcision with skill, force, and all their skill; but if the patient flees because of two or three towels, and by chance if one removes this one and leaves that one behind.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Or the wound covers again, and the pain is doubled, and at the movement which is done with too much force at the point of the limb; and at the movement of the tendon by chance escapes the iron, and repairs the work, and many times the nails are born again without having to make another incision, and I want that.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is equally taut throughout, but the thread is well twisted around the skin; and if the movement is slight at the outset, as if you were making the child understand, if he understands, do not force the thread more than to bind the thread around the limb slightly; then do it carelessly in every way you can; then hold it straight between your hands or between your thumbs and index fingers; then bring your hand to the limb and breathe out or cough, and move the limb up as high as the head of the limb is bent; then bind the limb firmly with the dirt that is collected; then tie the mark with a double thread, and tie it down once more; and hold the thumb against the pouch and the little finger against the index finger; then keep the thumb out of the way and bring the head of the limb back down; then leave the blood to clot naturally; for that is the best. And put powder on and over the powder a bandage glued with egg yolk from a fresh hen, confirmed with rose oil and balsam, and leave it on until the other wound is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the circumference is as follows: the two shoulders should be tense and depressed, and the arms as wide as the shoulder at the same time:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The wound of the mundane if it is when the spur of the abscess bursts at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your nail, even though it makes an incision; and hold it equally, and if you do not manage to hold your nail, if you keep holding, and then hold it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it transpires twice a day, and what is beside the rib is swollen, if you leave it as long as the abscesses diminish, and scorch it slightly; if you hold it as you wish, and keep it from the side of the rib, this will not help anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the liquid of things surrounding the wound with powder, that we have said or treated with powders, and if we hold it too long, it will go away, if it does not help; cure then, as we have said, until it is healed
dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The urine is retained if it is due to a stone, or blood clot, or bile, or worms, or other things which have been mentioned previously; and if the urine is not discharged, and you see that it is retained by the stone which is in the bladder, if it is possible, you must make the patient hunch his knees; and put his feet on the back, and extend his belly from the part under his back, and restrain the patient so that he cannot move as much as he can; and then bind the bladder neck to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is discharged; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, if it is possible, you must administer extraction with all the instruments which are called "syringes"; and this is the form: either of silver subtilized legier chest-high like a sparrow's beak; or the caine of a palm half-long; or subtilized at the chief.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus the method of extracting urine is as follows: if you take one double thread and bind one end to the head of a wool or cotton pad, and pass the thread through the syringe; and grasp the surplus of the wool and pass it up to the head of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or ointment and egg white, and make the patient sit on the chair; and raise the bladder and the flanks with oil moist and oily and warm water; then put the syringe gently into the flank, as far as it reaches the root of the flank; then double the flank upwards towards the buttock; then pull back the syringe until it reaches the bladder, and make the patient feel that the urine is coming out until the bladder is empty; this is not done except in the case that the urine is leading or going in another direction. Then draw up the thread to the very end of the wool and wool, and the urine follows the wool, then draw out the thread again, and correct the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are flank stones or blood in the bladder, or if there is swelling, and you see urine and medicines being distilled, if you have at your disposal the instrument called the «clepsedre», which is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped so that the medicine can be well impressed at the base, if we can drive out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see the medicines flowing in the bladder, put the chief dexter in the moisture, and drive out the one who is inside; if you drive out the moisture from the dexter, and then push strongly the one who is inside; if the moisture enters the dexter, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle fistula from which the bladder is closed.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from one armpit or the groin, then take a bladder of a kid and put the moisture in which you see closing the bladder, then bind it between the two armpits with a double thread, and burn one half of that moisture on the fire; then hold the chief of the fistula in the palm of the hand, and strain the hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has come into the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, if you take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round; then tie the thread strongly in these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a wheel, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and bind it with the instrument; and do as you would with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction along with medicines; and we have mentioned the difference between a stone that is incarcerated like a rain, and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be opened by size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and briefly.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is incarcerated in the bladder often occurs with vomiting, and this is a sign that the bladder is full of urine like a rain; and there appears gravel, and the patient groans with pain in the side, and he urinates many times, and then grows pale; and with these vomiting there is a foundation. And it is light to cure these vomiting until they are three years old; and it is very difficult in old people, and is as if one was mad between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first purify the patient by vomiting, to drive out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders to inquire about the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the limbs, and loosen and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; and let it never go upwards again; then make it sit between your hands as if they were clasped, and let its hands be at the sides of its thighs, so that the bladder is completely emptied downwards; then inquire and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut above the stone.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not yield to the toucher on all sides, put your left thumb on the abdomen of the patient, if the patient is female, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; and press downwards, inquire about the stone, and when you feel it on your middle finger, if the bladder is full; then press above your middle finger, and the stone will go out spontaneously or you will see it cut out.</start_of_turn
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the ribs above, and with his left hand to grasp the skin that is below the ribs in the part where the size is taken; then insert the spatula covering, since this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And go between that which is between the buttocks and the heel, do not put it in the middle but on the left side; and keep two hands on the stone, and two either above or below, and keep the size of the cut as if it were wide by force, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, do not put it too large; by chance the press if it must be above or below, that it leap forward in work; and thread that is in the hole or has angles, and margins: if it is grasped to stop; and if there is anything that is sweaty, resembles a gland, and round, from which issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there is an angle and margin on it, make the size greater; and if it does not jump, you must know that you must pull on the nails which are just like a file at the head, because the bone must be pulled if it escapes; or you can seize it with fine forceps at the head; and if you do not succeed in engaging it, if it is slipped, it is a bruise of vitriol; and if there are several stones, pull out the greatest one at the belly of the bladder first, then the middle, and the small ones afterwards if there are any
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is large, if it must be soothed, and make greater pain.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	If it is large, if it must be soothed, and make greater pain. For in this case two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out excessively because his wounds will not close; but whatever you do to try to mend them, or to remove the splinters, as long as you are tearing them out, until you have completed your work, if you employ incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and hold it, and put above a wet bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to appease the burning; then raise the patient up on his heel, and do not loosen the ligature until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have loosened it, if there arises much blood from the wound of oil and water, then treat with oily dynafinicon and oily basilicon, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	If swelling comes to the wound and corrosion, and blood clots in the bladder, and either because of this the urine is retained, which is known in part as a dry urine: then do you give two doses of urine in the wound and drain that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and bring it about. Then lift the wound with water and oil and bandage, and help him in every way you can until he is healed; and know that all the time you are treating him, that you must bind his two wounds together and assemble the medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the bladder or the urethra, and it is fixed, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician does this which I have said above, that you must lie down many times, we hear of the size for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already heard of this in other cases
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and make two angles fixed in one vessel:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then I take a thread and tie it around the base of the bladder and the stone, so that it does not go backwards into the bladder; then I pull the thread gently until it reaches the stone; and I push the thread towards my hand where the stone is and where it is not, until I can see the stone from the other side; when the urine comes, then I press my hand on that which remains of the stone that is inside the bladder
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the fracture is great, and if the patient leaps up with the urine, and if he cannot do this for any reason, then take a thread and pass it under the bone and another under, then pass the thread alongside the bone between the two lines, and grasp it with the forceps, and withdraw it slowly, and cleanse the wound with cold water; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you do not wish to do this by any means, take hold of the limb above the joint and support the limb below, then push the limb forward between the two tendons, and pull it out forcefully, remove the tendon, and congeal the blood that is in the wound; and cure as long as it is necessary.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	If the limb is ever dislocated in a woman, and if this has never happened before, then it is a serious cure, and is defended by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who is truly learned who knows how to manage such a thing, even though she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	If by chance a woman be not found who is well skilled in this work of hands; and if the bone of the woman be more deeply embedded than the bone of the man, for in this case more depth can be made, and great pain will follow. And if this be necessary, take a little knowledge that is well known, and prick the thumb, and if you do not find a vein, then do not attempt to take a vein from the woman; and present her with a well-skilled dance in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the work, and command her to do what you command her of concerning the inquiry of the bone; and look well whether the woman is a virgin: for in this case you can push out her shoulder or foundation and ask for the bone; and if she finds it, if you constrain her shoulder from her shoulder blade, and recommend that she bind her shoulder blade to the patient, and desire and press her left hand on her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If it be true, let her be moved from the groin to the knee, as far as she reaches the hip; then place your thumb on the hip at the root of the thigh, where it appears to be, and feel the hip in that part. Do not move her further from the hip or knee, but keep her small at first. Then bring her back to her normal size, if you feel the hip is eased from the wound as much as the hip can bear, and her discharge as many varieties of stones as there are: small and large, smooth and rough, long and round, and those which have rained.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if her discharge resembles stones, it is an issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if she does not improve, if you put on the thumb a bit of vitriol and keep it there for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the hip is firm, and have the instruments which I told you about in the extraction of the stone as home for you to aid in your work; and if she does not improve, and it is the artery that is cut, if you put on the powder on the limb and strain with pins and needles, and do not attempt it again; leave the limb alone and do not touch it, except by chance the patient dies. Then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the bleeding has ceased and the limb is at rest, if you return to this work while the wound is still fresh, as long as the bone is firm.</start_of_turn>
de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the intestines.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as soft as cheese, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it properly in the belly of the egg, if we take care that this is not the case. And this is the membrane of the cheese between the white fat that we have said.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this membrane is from weakness that comes from the cheese, and it is spread throughout that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if there is percussion on the bones, and this moisture if it has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and this is more; and these are signs of corruption in this assembly, for if it is yellow or white as we have said, if the abscess is renewed, I advise you to leave it as long as possible, and do not open the bones, because they are moist throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh, if the abscess is renewed with a part of the yolk, and because of this some people think that it is one and the same wound; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the white pith, if one feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it appears throughout the substance as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which comes after the introductor, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When we bind the wound with iron, if it be known that the patient is in good health and has a full recovery of his body; then we bind it on his back over something high, and put on him a cloth of draping; then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the limb up to the second rib of the costal cartilage; then we take the sponge, and cut the skin of the costal cartilage among the long bones as far as the prominence of the rib; and make our incision straight dividing the skin of the costal cartilage until we reach white tissue; and we burn the cartilage superficially as much as it is possible; then we pierce the cartilage plain with water to a large opening, and drain out all the fluid, and then put on our sponges, and retract the cartilage upwards; and do not touch the head of the ribs, but only the cartilage itself; cut all or in pieces immediately the cartilage surrounding it superficially, for if you do not cut it well it will return the fluid; and if the upper part of the rib leaps up towards your work, keep it in its place when you have finished the work on the cartilage. Then assemble the two leaves of the rib at a costure, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the blood corrupted by another illness, if you must tie up the veins that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then drain the wound thoroughly, and evacuate the blood, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If acute is assembled into two parts together, saeches that are two branches; if you press the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound a cloth soaked in rose oil; and put another cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and put on the two nails, and put beneath doubled cloths, and bind above all that is according to this fashion.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool like this in appearance and be assembled by stitching in the neck of the braies, and one of the nails grasps on the foundation almost to the back, and the other at the waist; and the other two heads on the two angles, and be all assembled the restriction in the loop of the arm; and never is medicine this branch of cautery instead of the size of iron, and take one needleful of cautery with a fine point, and prick the skin of the nails, and be scorched if as we have said, if the white substance that contains the blood is discovered; if you take the cautery like this form, and pierce that substance as we have commanded, and burn with this fine cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And take care in all ways that you can, until you have finished; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and be sure that this work is more salve; and keep guard of the bleeding, and more than the work of size; and if anything hinders you, or incisions or other things, if you can, cure what hinders you, as it is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, if he agrees to perforation, as I have said, and when you are certain by the meanings we have said that the aquouse root is lax, make the patient sit on a low chair; for pierce the abscess at the lower part with a wide needle, and put the perforation through to the bone; and let the wound be large enough for all the blood to drain; then put a wad over the wound, and bind it, and leave the remaining blood to drain away, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if white bile does not leave the wound, drink a drop or the instrument with which the blood is treated for hydrophobia, as it is said above; and enlarge the wound, and be sure the blood returns, and assemble after six months or when the pain has ceased, and when it is assembled as before, and then the patient will be able to pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Hairs that in this section of the twig are pale in many situations, for it seems to me that it is worth leaving them alone; and I will tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that abscesses often come from boils or corns, and sometimes from wounds; and this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by superfluous swelling and pain, which is spread like coions or percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the core; and there is no pain, and it is an abscess of grief; and by chance it is one abscess that is pale and bloody, and dark in color, and does not come from any artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from an artery, if it is known by the arrangement of the abscesses, when you press on it with your thumb; and it must not be touched by you
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his arrangement at the expression of the two thumbs, and can well make the size above this semblance, and above the other parts; and it is that you must seize like a thief, then the egg will be at the top, and the thread will be from white syph, and deliver the yolk from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already soaked with these hairs, if you must then draw the egg and seize it; and if it is on the syph, or in that which is in the vessels, if you must deliver all that is tense, and seize it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the limb hangs loose from the socket or from behind, then you must grasp all that is taut, and pull out the root, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is finished, if you have used up the soft wool dressing in oil and rose wine, then cure it with other ointments until it is healed.</start_of_turn
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering resembling a little sausage, with the softening of the hairs, and the patient groans greatly when he moves; and the cure for this disease is well known as much as this which is before us, and all that we say of it is the work of the ancient ones
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit upright on the edge of the seat, then support the suspended limb at the armpits by your sides, to all the vessels that are protruding from the groin, and grasp them firmly, and extend them forward; then pierce through the tough tissue with a large needle that will pass through the vessels, until they are discovered, and then withdraw it from the edge, as we have said in the extraction of arteries from the temples; then insert an awl or a double thread, and tie it at the first root or where the vein has come loose, and tie it at the other root; then close the wound steadily, according to the length of the bone, and remove the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as usual or apply a bandage, so that no vessel is left bleeding that has not bled during the incision; for in this way no harm will result, and if all the vessels are bled, as they will, it is permissible to remove the limb from all the vessels; if it does not lose its circulation from the incision of the vessels, and if it is dry and does not swell.
de la routure dou syfac	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	When the root of this herb comes to an end by fracture or tear, or extension on the belly in the region of the flanks, because the intestines descend from that passage to one of the buttocks; and that passage is either a fracture or an extension of the other, these two ways are the causes of vomiting: either from percussion, or from a jump, or from a blow, or from the raising of a bad grief, and by similar things; and the sign that this is an extension of the fracture is that there is some vomiting and some, with a long tension, does not come immediately; and the abscess is equal up to the navel, because the fracture presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the socket is inflamed, that it makes an immediate sharp pain, and the swelling is diverse, sometimes the skin is pale, and this is because of the escape of the intestine and the stiffness of the socket.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never is the bone moved with the intestine, and is retained when it is pressed, and makes great pain for the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with fire and fear, for it is known that they must be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	When the root of this herb comes to an end by fracture or tear, or extension on the belly in the region of the flanks, because the intestines descend from that passage to one of the buttocks; and that passage is either a fracture or an extension of the other, these two ways are the causes of vomiting: either from percussion, or from a jump, or from a blow, or from the raising of a bad grief, and by similar things; and the sign that this is an extension of the fracture is that there is some vomiting and some, with a long tension, does not come immediately; and the abscess is equal up to the navel, because the fracture presses the intestines.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the flesh except as we have said, after the incision, in doubt of the discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this matter, it often happens that blood flows out through an opening; and if it is delayed at the outset, if it be from a wound of hot water, put on what we have said, until it flows; then cure the wound by another means, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the intestines.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter, I have never seen anyone cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old people say that it is made like the twig which is bound to the nail, in part as if you bind up the veins, after the fashion of a wound that has been dressed too loosely; then pull them out a little, and cure the abscess of that which caused it, until the veins flow; and cure it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes rupture in anger, as we have said, and open the eyes; and do not touch any intestines as you would a sausage, and if you do, it is too late, and repair at all hours; and all this if it stays too long in this place, if you believe the wound or tumor, until the intestines are evacuated; and this comes from the stretching of the flesh in anger, as we have said, because it is swollen, then is softened and relaxed the eyes and open; and cure it if by cautery, as we have said before; and never is cured with iron in this manner: and that the patient lies perfectly still on his back between your hands, then pull out the limb of the rupture inflated with the width of three fingers; and then draw out the tumor which is below the skin, and take hold of the root and take it out, pressing on the belly, then cut out the two ends of the tumor from the root, and cut one and the other; and then draw out the root, and do not touch the tumor or stretch the navel or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestine twig; and cure it by the wound cure.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cauterize the hair, if the wound closes and heals the wound, as long as it is whole.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is confined, and has no apparent cause in the course of treatment, and the cautery is useless in this situation, and more proximate to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the nails is softened in baths of warm homes, because the nails that are within become softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to remove the softened skin from the natural skin; then assemble the layers together with a suture, and if you see, sew up the excess of softened skin at two or three sutures firmly; then close between the sutures, and cure as with the other wounds, until it is healed, and take out the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	The boils that we learned in our law are sufficient for our purposes; and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book. It is only necessary in two instances: the first is that the patient should be questioned about the boil’s response when requested, and should be treated for the boil; and the second, because we have often seen bestes being castrated for our assistants, as with goats and sheep, cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do it by traction, we seat the beast in warm water, until the testicles are softened and limp; then we grasp them with our hand, until they are put back and you no longer feel them
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the burn: Command that you hold the best hand, and press the skin of the nails to your left hand, then bind the suspension, and put a compress upon each wound twice when you have well secured them; and leave no mark of needle or silk which is outside the vessels; and this method of burn is more severe than that which is done by traction, because at traction remains by chance no hair of the nails, because the best desire luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways as at home: one if between the two nails appears as with the figure of nature a woman, or if there are hairs, and sometimes in court it urinates.

de la tentigene	Hermofrodie is according to two ways: one if between the two testicles opens as with the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in between they urinate. Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenacity is a garlic clove placed on the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have had as much as with a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to hold the excess of the tenacity at your hand or on the armpits, and to grasp it lightly; and do not press too much, for blood will not come out, but rather the cure will come from another cure while it is still whole; and there is another remedy that comes from the root of the marigold, and the lobe, and by chance it spurts forth, and this is called the ancient "coward's disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you perceive that it has slipped, as we have said, hold the limb steady until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If the limb is dislocated because of its natural position is not recognized, or if the wound is small; or if it is by birth, or caused by illness, or by a severe bruise, or a bite from a dog, or a wound in the marrow, or on the coasts, or on bones, or anything similar; then you must recognize the fracture, and the child, and by chance the flowers to have; and knowledge of this comes from experience.</start_of_turn>
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If swelling appears nearby, if you wish to test the two limbs or the root.</start_of_turn

If there is a wound in the marrow, and it is close to the liver, if you are in a hurry, and the limb is broken: put your two index fingers together, and let the patient lie on their back, spread their legs; then pull the two levers apart, as long as the bony bruise is round, and is over the swelling; then take oil and poultice, and put it on the wound, and keep the patient still in bed until the swelling subsides.</start_of_turn

des emorroides	des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes are bursts of veins which, without external support, customarily lead to swelling; and when old, become tough. And as we have said in the preceding chapters concerning the signs and symptoms, I will now mention those which resolve with cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that in old emboli, when they are softened in the marrow, and cannot be felt, if they are not treated by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the root of the marrow can be felt, and these can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it sticks, that is good.

des apostemes de la marris	Emorroids are tears in veins which without support are not usually seen; and when old become tough. And we have said concerning the marks and signs, I will say here those which are useful for cure. I say that emorroids and tough veins, when they are pressed in the marrow, and they are not felt, if not except by the cure by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the heel and press on its root, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw its pieces an hour later, and put it in cold water; and if there is blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix with honey and assails, and make one application on her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is an opening at the back, and there are clots that look like wounds; then take lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make an opening at the root. And when the wound is healed, if it is cured of swelling as long as it is healthy; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if it is covered as I have said the tough veins; and then it is cured as long as it is healthy.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come into the marsh, such as carbuncles and perforated abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and cautery abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the previous division.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is proper that I say that when the burn comes to the marrow which is in the heel, it is not of the kind which adheres to the bow; and if you know the work of iron, look if the burn is already in the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, you shall know.

Do not be in a hurry, but make me measure as long as the pain is eased; then make the patient sit on a chair, and give him two little chairs or stools, and support him on his back and join his limbs together; and let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms across his knees, and bind them securely with a bandage; then draw out the ball towards the breastbone, and bring the instrument with which we open the heel, from which the form will follow; and know that when you bring this instrument, that you must first feel the depth of the heel, so that what comes between the instrument and the bottom does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is proper to cover the depth of the heel with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause him pain; and it is proper to put the horn of the instrument at the bottom, and hold the instrument.

de l’enfantement	De l’enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The peasant is first at the fair when he knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down on the navel, and desire to smell the armpits: then the child comes out head first; and if the child's birth is according to the natural figure, and comes out headfirst, and is seconded by it; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on his belly, if the child comes out headfirst, for when he descends on his head, if he is seconded by it, and the mother is amazed at his superfluities by his good birth. Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are they formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV; and they are all formed like a child by the measure of the glorious sage, and it is to be known that in this way similar things happen; if you do as it is commanded.</start_of_turn
de l’enfant mort	From childhood death.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman of a dead child or of a belly, if as I have said in the division, and it does not come out violently, and you are constrained by the work of your hands; if you believe that the woman is of sound mind, and has no accident or is not in danger of death; if you believe that the woman is lying on her back, and her shoulders are flexed forward and her legs are raised; and you touch her with two fingers, or bind her to the bed if she is not to be treated at the descent of the child; then wipe the mouth of the woman with oil mixed with alum and fenugreek seeds and linseed; then anoint her hands with these oils and these substances; then put them in the belly lightly; then give her something to drink or the things she is accustomed to; and beware that the child does not rise up on his head; if he stretches the ointment in his eyes or in his nose or in his mouth or on his beard or in his mustache or on his chest, and if he rises up on his toes, he will grip or pinch and groan; and you must keep the ointment at his right hand, and put the elbow between his two left fingers, and hold his hand lightly, and pinch the ointment in no place that we have said, until it comes to the end of the matter. And that is the form of the ointment:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then the hair is found one other on the skin, or the third is mixed in, if so be the extraction equal; and then stretch them equally by moving from one side to the other, for mucus is to be extracted, or the nails are to be held by means of the hands, as is the fashion.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains, if one sees a little of its fat around its belly, and press it to that part, and treat the other part; and if there is still some remaining, if put this hair or higher up again, and do so until it is all gone
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be pulled back due to the stretching, then you must know that you must cover over the drape, until it is whole; then bring the thumb into the joint of the wrist or the heel, and then you must do the same with the other hand, and hold the two feet together.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the shoulder is large and is twisted at the joint, or if there is much pain in the shoulder blade assembled, if you must stretch the spinous process between your two thumbs, and press down on the pain; or you may bind it with the instrument which is called the "almidach," which comes with the instruments or chapter which follows this one; and thus make the limb naturally flexible; and then draw the bones apart, and the dislocation will be forced out, if it can be forced out by force, until the moisture which is either coming out or remaining comes out; and if it cannot be driven out, if the bone is fractured, as much as the moisture that is coming out or remaining; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, if you must pierce as much as the moisture corrects.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if it is swollen above its feet, if the attraction is slight, and the movement towards the mouth of the marrow is less arduous.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is swollen in the belly or the arm, it is proper to grasp the hand that covers the area; and press the belly or the arm until the moisture that is there is expelled. If another limb is stiff and the head of the joint remains immobile, if the limb is grasped by the thumb and pulled toward the mouth of the thumb, and the thumb is treated until it reaches the second or third knuckle, and if the mouth of the thumb is closed by a thick scab that has come away, if it is not possible to pass anything through, it is proper to administer oily and greasy things; and to administer poultices, and soak in hot and soothing water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.
