If the fetus lies on its chest, and you put it in its proper position, if you administer what we have said concerning the living child; and if that does not suffice, if you must force it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	When you have done this, if anything like what we have said above happens in the marsh, and blood comes from the wound, if it is put into a restraining liquid, and other cures are added.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb two infants were conceived, and as soon as one was born, the other expelled it.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came a swelling in her belly, and it burst open, and it began to swell greatly
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I called for help, and I thought for a long time, and I could not stop the bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong dressing, and blood came out, and after a while another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at mouth, for this belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I saw the wound open wide, and hands broken, until the woman was greatly better; and I saw the woman long tense with fear, and that was almost the end of her; and I have never remembered this chapter except for this, that when the master found a strange thing, he had to seek help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of the pressor, as we have read in the books; and there are two returns with two thumbs of the two fingers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horn or the restriction should be more subtle, or made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the vessel should be wide open, and the margin of the trees should be long, and for a palm and a half; and between these two limbs there should be two supports of the same substance, which are closed in one and the other, half palm or more; and these two supports are placed in the mouth of the vessel to open when the two horns are turned
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails; and has two arms two inches long, and two broad; and when you see the uterus open with all the instruments, make the woman sit with her legs together and her feet apart, then place the two arms of the instruments together in the uterus, and hold the handle of the instruments between her thighs; then grasp your hand with all the instruments, if you have made the nails even, according to the quantity you see open the mouth of the uterus, until the belly makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very sharp, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when one beholds them appear, the work hastens, and the height of one's home increases in proportion.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If one does not fear the instrument except when it appears, for its need is not easily dispensable
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second stage is retained in infancy, if you command the patient to hold back her breath, and then make her cough forcefully, and grasp her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she spits out because of that, that is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take I pot and make I hole or cut, and put herbes in it that can open the mouth of the mare, as with calamus, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbes, or any of them, be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a salve or hole in the pot, and the other head in the mouth of the mare, and hold until the vapor comes out of the mare; then make her cough, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint downwards is affected.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this cure and there is no further cause, as I command at the dance, she moistens her left hand with oil of sesam or in alabaster ointment, and then puts it back in the nature, and desires the second one; and when she has found it, if she grasps and extends it forward and backward, so that the mare does not cry out at the extraction; but it is necessary to move her slightly to the left and right, and then treat her. If she comes and becomes quiet.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the mare is swollen, as we have said, the cure is to stop eating and fumigate with herbs; if this does not suffice, keep that you do not eat; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the mare be bound to the woman's hip, and then be cauterized with oil of tetrafarmacon; if she drinks and recovers, it will go well; however, if she drinks and there comes a bad odor from the stomach and head, and vomiting, it will harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it be certain that such fumigations are useful in this case: neither of the former has proved the fumigation of rosemary and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument in which we fumigate the woman at the retention of flowers and the secondine if it be this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like seeing a fox, and put the head of the patient over the fire; and either fumigate over charcoal, and keep it going until it is exhausted, and do it again.</start_of_turn>
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the firm foundation of perception, and they are stifled by a subtle stiffness: if you can therefore give to the dance that she pierces that stiffness at its root, and do not prick her with an acute spathe, and keep the dressing that she does not touch; then put on moist cloth in wine and oil, and the cure of oil until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, if you put or withdraw a sponge of lead, and leave your hands free, and be patient as long as the child sees the wound alert in bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Never comes this sudden stamping of the wound or the incision; if you cover that stamping: if it be cured, as we have said of the sponge of lead.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that arise from below the foundation are nodes, and those that arise from above the foundation are liable to burst, or in the middle of two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when the node is old, if it is above, and is accompanied by moisture, white or yellow pus, these fistulas are never permanent; and are known by the patient when he passes feces or experiences vomiting or flatulence.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and halfway up the thigh; and reach as far as the joint of the hip, and beyond the navel.</start_of_turn>
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus it is known that a fistula that arises from the foundation is not permanent; and that when you bite your thumb or the foundation, and insert a fine needle or iron awl into the fistula when there is no swelling.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is swelling, if you insert a sponge or a horsehair, as long as you feel the swelling or the swelling persists; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of feces or vomiting or flatulence, as we have said: such discharge does not pierce; if you are in a hurry to cure it
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists until the bladder or the urine duct, if in a leap the urine escapes, and cannot be retained by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived up to the hip joint, if it is the vein that is coming up to the limb; if there is no twisting and the pain is only at the start, if it has gone back to its place, and there is no medicine or support to be done by ointment; and in these fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of fools who interfere with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one which is not sudden and is not old, there is hope of healing by fire, as I have experienced; and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and that you pull the legs up to the hips, and that you incline the hips towards the belly; then attempt to pull out, or plunge if there is twisting, until you have drained or the attempt comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain at the root of the index finger, if you believe he has injured it; whether it is torn or you sense between his thumb and index finger a swelling or bulge, then pull out the nails that are causing the swelling; if you do not extract them, it will not heal.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We cannot heal anything without pain, but this is often the case; and the help we give is to scald the cautery superficially as much as the size of the fistula allows, as it is said above; and we fill the cavity with ointment, until it reaches below the root; and do this two or three times until you are sure that these nails that must be burned out are burned; which resemble a bundle of hairs; and then we cauterize the wound with soft tucks, until the nails are gone, then we dress the wound with oil and bandage.</start_of_turn>
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is still sane, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is still sane, that is good; for if he tries and does not pierce until he reaches the marrow or foundation, and between his thumb and index finger he puts on a thick covering of hair or chaff, and you see the fistula arise from beneath the covering like a worm; if he grasps the edge of the fistula and pulls it out before he tries again, and then burn the cautery afterward, as long as it comes up to the top of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered and will heal. Then cleanse away the hair that appears like a bundle of feathers, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he will not go without force, and if you are between him and the work, if you cauterize with fire or medicine that is strong.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, two things are assembled: namely, the burning of these hairs that grow, and the constriction of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of soft wounds covered in fat or chopped bones, until they bleed profusely, and is sufficient to burn the hair in the wound; then cure the wound of running sores with dry chaff, and these are the dry medicines
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is well and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	When it is restored, if it is well and does not return, and if a fistula comes up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if the thumb or the root is moved, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If thou feel the attempt, and between two thou art in the toile or the syfac or the char, or it is near to pierce, if there be no other means but flight and hope, by the administering of one of these three ways: either thou cauterize it as we have said, or thou bind it until it be healed, or if thou wilt thou may pull it out if thou puttest thy hand to it; but do not be too hasty, that thou cover not the foundation which holdeth the wound, and bring forth the discharge in the right direction; then cure it as we have said; by chance if it be sound, or thou remove the covering and the matter then that it is bound from the foundation, or by attempt or by other pointed instrument; then defend that which is in the wound as thou wilt; then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula at the part following the foundation: if it be a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either cost or situated deep under the skin, if you take a bite pierced at the head in this fashion:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And there is always a thread torn in two, and you must pull the attempt all the way through the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either cost or situated deep under the skin, if you take a bite pierced at the head in this fashion: if it is present at the base of the wound, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your wound or the base; and draw out the head of the thread, and reunite the two ends together, and constrain one to the other, and leave it one or two; and do not restrain at any time, until the thread has closed these holes which are between the two, and has ceased to bleed; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, if you force it to pierce in every way you can, it will not be too much.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to force it too tightly with the stitches, and then cure it as we have said, while it is still healthy.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny bladder from which the fistula is made is moist and one-sided, part and trenchant; and on the other hand not, forasmuch we must not pierce this one that we must not pierce, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you wish to bind the shoulder according to this manner: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through from below and pull the needle through again, and twist two threads of the thread around the needle, and if it is thick; strain the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and make sure of all the others, and leave one to correct the excess blood; then put on the foundation a moist drape in oil of roses or cerote, and put on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until it blanches, and when it is white, if the wound of the oil and other remedies is complete, while he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when the fire is finished or the foundation is firm</start_of_turn>
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	There are often dry fevers in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is not worth.</start_of_turn
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice that a swelling has formed at the edge of a nail or at the nail itself, which does not allow it to moisten; then treat it until it is healed if it is possible; and if it does not heal, if you must, repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until the wound bleeds, and is scraped away; then treat it until it is healed
dou fremit	indeed.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small hairy outgrowth that appears before the limb, and goes down the limb like a burr; and never does it leave the trueve without leaving a mark, and it is felt just like death from fear, and comes to the whole limb, and more is in the hands than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure for this is that you take a quince of goose feather, or a quince of strong vulture feather, and put that quince on the wound, until the circle turns blue around the wound; then twist your hand with all your might until you pull out the wound all the way, and put it back down, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is done with a needle or iron in this fashion, and be discreet of your steps and cautious of your hands.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see that it is done with a needle or iron in this fashion, and be discreet of your steps and cautious of your hands, do not pierce, for it must be held firm, and must be pressed. And if you see that you have cauterized too far forward or behind the cautery, stop immediately.</start_of_turn>
de la forme dou clistere	And if you see that it is done with a needle or iron in this fashion, and be discreet of your steps and cautious of your hands, do not pierce, for it must be held firm, and must be pressed. And if you see that you have cauterized too far forward or behind the cautery, stop immediately.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	And never make a blister of silver or gold, or of lead or tin; and never make of these instruments petty and great, according to these to which they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the treatment of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if it is due to a wide belly, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is swelling or the belly is bound, if you see, and if the shoulder is pulled out either from front or back; and if there are two holes on one rib, and one on the other; or if the belly or an organ has medicine in a bladder or parchment, or if it is pierced all around with fine needles, and there is one inch of space between each needle, then insert into these holes one strong thread of coarse thread twisted in the shape of an X or around, and assemble the belly like a key; and when the medicine is inside, if there is a suture in front of a strong thread, then clip it; and that is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold; anoint the head with oil or balm of eggs, or something similar; then bind it lightly; then grasp the hand of the minister with both hands, until it is quite visible; then draw out the blister, and leave the patient his legs exposed, and if the medicine wishes to see, if he can manage; and if he sleeps throughout the night, if it is more effective.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he sees it in the disease of falling of the belly, and the physician hastens to go out, if he recommences as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bruising or swelling, or an abscess, if the blister is as subtle as for one child; and this is the form of a subtle blister that is on the skin, and not strained
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in this section the treatment of wounds; or rather the treatment of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on the way they are made, and depending on the parts of the body from which they are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are biting of stones, or the size of a spear or nail, or an arrow or lance or sickle, or similar things; or that are made in accordance with the laws of herbs, as for wounds that bleed from the neck, or the head, or the face, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for a simple wound, and we will begin with the wounds of the head alone, because the memory will come to mind in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a fracture occurs, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that there is no spitting of stones or other things, and the skin is thoroughly ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt about a tetanus shot: if you do so immediately after the wound, even if there is blood from the wound itself, or on the contrary side; and listen to the patient’s swelling of wine and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he does not recover, if he vomits meat and does not drink wine or eat meat; and put out the wound, if tetanus comes, soak linen cloth in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no tetanus shot, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, except that I will tell you later; and if it has been moved, put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a nail and similar, and the layers do not want to stick together by tension, if you join them together with stitches, as I will say for wounds on the belly, from the stitches.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by the bone, it is wide open and will not stay closed except at a point; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you find or split skin at the bone, if it does not touch the bone, if you can pull it out whole, and it oozes pus, then cauterize it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be staunched by medicine, if you find it severed, if you pull it out with a thread; and if this does not help, if you must, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if the cure is legitimate: put on this powder which binds just as well as if it had moved them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and grind them together finely; and apply them to the wound, and hold it firm, until it heals well and joins together again; and then bind it well, and leave it loose, if it does not swell; for one does not harden the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we make this charcoal burn only, when we have no incense or blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has moved from its place, even if it is in this state, if one does not put on my plaster; but put on some unguents digested, or poultices of oatmeal made of water and honey, until it has secreted enough; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If a fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, if the bone is grasped with fine tweezers; and I will tell you later about larger fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the head.</start_of_turn>
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes with the head and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the neck or the artery is cut.</start_of_turn
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, if there is no other ailment except to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restraining, because it hinders the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything rough on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of blood is with the brain, which is the most important limb; but if the medicine is severe, like molten chalice in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and poppy seeds washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this method, and moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if the bone and the surrounding tissue are bent, then cure it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and the swelling is great and full of pus, if the wound is near a bone or artery; if the artery is severed, there is discharge of blood; if the swelling and the pus mix together; and if the epiglottis or the tonsils are severed, or the windpipe is damaged, the meat will go down, if the windpipe is cut on the side of the throat, and do not touch the throat but replace it as it naturally lies; and then strain it out immediately, and leave it alone for some days, then cure it with oil until it is healed; and if there is a piece of bone in the wound, if the fragments of bone break off, do not try to take them out; leave them in as long as the wound persists, and evacuate and align the issue.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the cure be as I have said in this chapter.</start_of_turn
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of from a wound of lance or knife</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be of spear or knife, and the wound is deep, if thou seest the wound has burst forth, know that the wound is mortal; and if it be not deep and it is fresh throughout, if thou dost not put in at the first hour the powder, neither bind it up with the blood, but restore the patient, and give him rest; but put in an astringent, and bind it twice firmly; and if thou dost not have an astringent, put in the wound some coarse cotton to absorb the moisture, and cause the patient to sleep upon the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there be no spasm, neither tremor of body nor straining of the bowels. When thou seest the bones disposed, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tonsils and other cures, as long as they are sane; and if they cannot be cured, and if there is an opening, drain the pus that has formed; as is proper.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or knife, and it is simple, or worse on the front or back, if the treatment of what is before is sufficient; if it is large, suture it; if it is small, dust it; and if it is close to bone, break off pieces, if necessary for the wound, and drain the pus if it is purulent; and if it is not purulent, leave it to heal naturally; and in other wounds, the judge will know what to do as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	as other limbs are the judge of such things as we have said.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The fall of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound no time the intestines do not go out, or the nerves of the intestines, because of the introduction of feces; and the suture is more painful, and no time is better than a little wound than a great one, because in this way one can bring the intestines back in one by one; for as soon as they feel the fruit, they go back in one by one; and for this reason the lesser wound is better than the greater, because it brings the intestine back to its place as well as the others. And the pus that comes out of the belly is according to four methods: the two common sutures are in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds is common to other wounds; and all of them are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say one word and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is pressing, and only a little thing is protruding, this can be remedied in two ways: either by the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak the area partly: moisten a sponge or I put a wet drape over it only, or you bathe in hot water squinting and clapping and pricking, and elevate the intestine until it has become firm; and do not do this treatment too tightly, and be quiet that you do not make it swell further.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or is cooked and the veins are burnt, for by this is the entrance aligned with the things; and if it cannot enter, if make a wound the wound at the instrument to grasp the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is quiet that the size, that we must not cut without great necessity or have no need; and this is the instrument for cutting: if you dig inside the curve and pull out no further, and when this is done, shape it.</start_of_turn
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen and the intestines protrude, if you stop bleeding in accordance with the natural form in its own place, you will have done well, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large and is in the lower part of the belly, if you must manage the patient on his back and raise his legs above his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put his head and shoulder higher than the lower parts, and so if the round belly is in one of the two lower parts, put your hand on that which is higher than the other; and thus you must bring about what I have said in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put your thumb between your hands and hold all the edges together; and that is the common way of stitching, and take a needle or more according to the size of the wound, and leave the end of the wound free; and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the needle, which is from the inside of the skin, until you have pierced it through that part, and assemble the two ends of the skin together; then strain a double thread around the needle at two parts, and assemble the two ends of the wound again, and then leave a space, and pierce another needle; and tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease doing so until the whole wound is held together; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and coarse, for the fine needles will grasp all the substance, and the too coarse will not penetrate well: for this reason you must make them moderate; and do not force the needles too much against the substance and the skin, for they will not grasp and will open the wound before the suture; and then grasp the ends of the needles, that they do not stain the patient at sleep, and put patches or dressings over the holes of the needles for a while to hold them, and leave them as long as the wound is healing; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there is only one needle or two of the second kind that is common, and that you assemble the two ends of the skin and the two ends of the needle together with a needle or there is a strong thread in the middle. And when you have pierced these things together, strain the needle at the part or where you began, in the manner that you cut the threads; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a minor thumb; this stitch is useful for a wound that has occurred from a cut or the belly, which was swollen from a knife, and the wound was larger than a palm of a great hand, and there were intestines well two palms of great, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will restore the gut when it has been outside for twenty-four hours, and it was closed for fifteen days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they thought the patient was going to die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with medicine, for I was in a place where there was none, neither medicine; and I put oil on the wound twice a day, and bathed it with honey until it healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me two ways to suture: take the needle and pass it through the lower part until it reaches the top; when it has pierced the outer edge on the right side, if the tissue is slack or strained or if you have passed the needle, withdraw the needle and pass it through the lower part until it reaches the top; and you understand this stitching if you suture like a leatherworker and leave one hole open on one side and then pass the needle through from the other side until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does so discreetly, if it is so with none else, which joins the two parts naturally, and brings one of the chief close to the other chief, in this manner: pierce a needle or chief close to the next, and make it pierce only that which is below, and leave the two chiefs of the syfac; then turn the needle and make it pierce from the back side until it reaches the middle, having two chiefs of the syfac; then make it pierce one and the other from the back side until it reaches the middle, in two other chiefs of the syfac that are on the other side; and that is the wisest method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says this himself, and no one testifies against him; we must sew the belly with two needles, or there is yarn in the seam; and we must pass one needle through from one side, and the other through from the other side, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and the stitches that when the gut is turned inward, if the suture is finer than others in the gut.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like that of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestine and its cost, then put on the healing powder. If it has moved, do not put on anything other than what is present until the wound is healed; and close the wound, and be certain of the stitches, the suture, and the dressing. Then cure the wound like the others until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, put on nothing until it starts to ooze blood, cotton wool, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You do not need any other medicine for many wound dispositions than for simple wounds. If you doubt whether the wound will heal properly, moisten coarse linen with warm olive oil or rose oil, and put it on the wound edges. Wash the area. If there is pain or decay in the bowels, and this happens often, if the cluster of black vomit is given to you, and even if the decay reaches the intestines; pierce it through and drain what is in it, especially if it is the large intestines, as it is easier to heal than the small intestines.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot heal when they are swollen, because of the swelling of the veins, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the wound bursts, if it is reset backwards as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or dark, if you tie the black part, since there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the edges, and suspend the two ends of the wound from the part below the wound until the bursting is aligned, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	because of the wound
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, if it can be restored in small wounds, because I have seen that one bone was swollen or swollen by an arrow; and the wound was at the side of the stomach, and became filled and became a fistula, and in this there was evacuation and vomiting; I treated it as I thought fit, and I did not cease to soften it until it was healed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has nothing wrong in his belly; and there is no point of wrong, but much better arrangements, and food and drink; and they say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be ligated in parts: take tweezers of great capacity, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the tweezers have passed over the mouth, if the latter has gone beyond, put two lips back, so that it tears its mouth above; and then close the wound, and this is kept if it does not slip, and put another tweezers afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is whole; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	When the gut is perforated and there is no other nuisance to the patient, and it is possible to ligate the gut with a fine wire which is cut from the gut of a beast, in parts: take the head of this wire of gut that is cut out, and then tie to the head of this wire one thread of fine linen twisted, and pass the thread through the needle, and sew up the gut, and hold it in its place; and this manner of stitching with tweezers is not fierce except as regards the way of engagement and expectation; and if the wound is great and wide, as it is in one of the large intestines, except for slightness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or that it is a fistula, or that it is simply
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds and abscesses, when they swell, if they are called universally "fistula", and even when they are closed and swollen.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is a wound that swells and cannot be closed; it is called a fistula throughout. Sometimes it is as wide as a bird's quill; sometimes it is wide open, sometimes it is narrow, sometimes it is thick, sometimes it is thin; sometimes it is little, sometimes it is great; I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, for every wound that is not healed, and there is pus, is only cured by one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or the hardness of the flesh; or by its wickedness; or because there is too much pus inside and outside; or because the wound is too wide; or because the flesh is relaxed and the matter is of bad quality; or because the medicine is not good at the cure; or because the corruption is like that of a pestilence; or because the property of the region is late in digestion and in healing, and runs away by nature; or because there is a vein or a bone involved. And I have already mentioned all these causes and their signs and cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you must know that I shall tell you of the cure for fistula, which is made by an operation of the hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Hair that has become inflamed has occurred in all limbs with pain; for there are fistulas that arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the spleen, or intestine, or bladder, or in some of the bones, or at the shoulder blade, or at no joint of the hands or feet; and if one part has come to the property of the principal limb, and the rest remain.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All the fistulas of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is no fistula that does not go deeper than I have said, and you have assumed there is a cure, and you see it improve, if one attempt to cauterize it when it is straight, if it is so; and if it is crooked, if the surrounding tissue attempts to sink, for it swells inward toward the curvature; and if the fistula is through and through, and you do not well cauterize it with attempts, if it bursts through one of the perforations, for the moisture is too close from one perforation to the other, and it softens; then when it is dry again, you must know if there is bone or nerve, and it is chewed out of place, and ask the patient of the pain he feels at the touch of your hand, and where it is; and when you know truly where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in some of the things I have told you, if the incision agrees with what I have said, and the bone is forced out and the corrupt parts that are within; and then the cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep from the outset, if you can force them out as well, then put in gentle attempts with medicine that is wet, and keep them until the medicine consumes the superfluousness that is remaining; and then put on nourishing ointments that are safe, until it is healed. And if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, if the incision agrees.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or principal nerves are not swollen or affected, and if the bone is discovered to be fractured, and there is corruption and blackness, if the fracture extends as long as the corruption is throughout the bone, then cure the thing with external supports as long as it is sane; and if it is not sane, and the pain persists as before, extract the bone until it is sound; and if it is sound, it is well done.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, extract the bone if the corruption is too great to bear; if there is no other remedy except to let it remain as it is by nature; and if there is a small bone that is fractured, and you wish to treat it, do so with a suitable instrument, and if there is any remaining bone, leave it whole; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no doubt or fear, bind tightly with moisture and support, and deliver the bone.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you do not remove the offending matter at an opportune hour, if you place something absorbent over the wound and leave it until the pus has dried up around the bones, then the bones will become less painful. And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, if you keep the corruption so slight that the blackness is throughout the bone, then restore the wound. And if there is a great part of the bone corrupted, and you must remove a portion of the bone; if you cover it with silk and cover everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I shall tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man’s leg, so that you may learn from it and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about the age of thirty who had pain in his leg due to something within the bone, until the matter came out at the knee. He fled from a large abscess, but did not know the cause of the abscess; but he came to his senses when he saw the abscess break open so that it opened up as much as the abscess itself, and pus came out of it, and it became a fistula. And from that there was loss of blood and moisture from the bone; and he remained like that for two years, and there was no skill in his hands, as I learned when I went back to see him, and saw his leg and the medicines which they were using, and what was causing the pain in the bone; and the bone became red from the pain, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I bound a thread in one of these holes, and then encircled all the holes, and found that one followed the other throughout the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I thereupon bound up one of the holes and found part of the bone broken and rotten, and the corruption spread to the marrow; I excised all that appeared to be corrupted, and I thought that there was no further corruption, except for that which I had already removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but I could not staunch the bleeding; and then I repeated the process, and again found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I excised it, and then fixed it, and I thought I had cured it. But as I bound around the thumb, the thumb bled profusely, and I had to remove the bandage altogether, and only then did the bleeding stop. And he was healed and sound, and never bled again except for the weakness of the patient, who was unable to endure it, and for fear of death which I had averted for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.
