For often there is the evacuation of blood, but he remained entirely well; and in place of the bone there grew a hard scale, and it was of good fortune and caused no hindrance or any adversity in any way, neither to the spirit nor to the body.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no limb whatsoever, if you wish to suture in this manner: take I thread, and pass it through the chief of the bone that breaks, and command no one to extend it upwards; and put I another thread of linen thicker than the first, and bind it over the scale which is detached from the bone, and extend the chief, so that you tear out the corrupted scale at the bottom, and uncover the scale above the place where you see the suture, that the thread does not split the scale; and put I a sponge or a tab of alum at the bottom of the bone to cover the corrupted scale; and suture as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and suture again.</start_of_turn>
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not yield to the touch, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, if you uncover the whole limb; then put on a pair of gloves, and then join the corruption from one end to the other; and be sure to join for as long as the corruption lasts; and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint, join the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, if there is no other vein than that which covers; and if the corruption is at the wrist or the elbow, if it is strong in that thing, but all the same you must inquire about that corrosion, how it happened to you; and mitigate it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not oppose; and that the incision and the sutures cover these bones many times, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of wounds, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and durability. And for this reason it is necessary to appear with some semblance of work; and that the work will show you the instrument that you must have, according to your knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of diseases.
dou feu	If you think of the instrument which you must employ in this case, according to what it is able to do.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated by swelling, by pressure from within, or by violence; and when you have treated the cause of the dislocation with medicine, but it has not profited, if you cover that limb until the swelling subsides, or if the cause of the dislocation persists, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by the greater malice of the defect of the limb; the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and afterwards comes the blackness, because that corruption of the limb spreads throughout the limb and takes hold of the whole body; if you delay covering, and if it is by the percussion of venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea, vipers and the like, if the corruption is at the root of the bone, if you do not give it space to come out until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	When it comes to the hand, if the swelling has reached the joint, if the corruption has not progressed further than the forearm; if it has reached the forearm, if the swelling has progressed to the upper arm; if it has reached the upper arm, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the extent of its power; and do all that you can do when the corruption comes or goes: if it comes in the first joint, if the swelling comes after the other; and if it comes or goes, if it swells the whole limb; if it rises in the leg, if it swells at the knee; and if it comes below the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and to cover the limb with a bandage from below and above, and to stretch one minister across the lower part of the limb and another minister across the upper part, and to uncover the part between the two ministers to a span of one spittle wide, until the bone is exposed; then cover or uncover the swelling and put a bandage over the drape of linen, so that the swelling does not touch the sound limb, and cause the patient further damage and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes from the wound when working, if you cauterize the limb hastily, or put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accompanied by something; then bind the limb securely with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a case in which this happened: there was a blackness that seemed to burn like fire in the bone; and this corrosion began in the middle of the bone, until it consumed the whole bone; and when we saw the corrosion, if we did not cover the bone, it healed; and when the bone returned to its normal position, the corrosion recurred again; and I had to cut off the limb. I did not want to hope to recover the matter; and I believed that if I cut off the limb, he would die, because the man’s strength was weak; and he awoke, returned home, and covered his limb, and was healed; and I have never heard of such a case except for this one, where it was necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes abscess in the limb and remains so long that it makes great swelling of the bow; then it returns and breaks, and in the leap of the bow, and remains limp, as a vessel; and the leather that is under is as subtle as a draped veil, and does not reach the bone, neither the nerve, and such an ailment is called "blood clot", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone embedded in the flesh, it is called "fistula"; and if the leather is that you can grasp that leather all around, and even when it is subtle, as a draped veil; and it does not move from its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	Never comes abscess in the limb and remains so long that it makes great swelling of the bow; then it returns and breaks, and in the leap of the bow, and remains limp, as a vessel; and the leather that is under is as subtle as a draped veil, and does not reach the bone, neither the nerve, and such an ailment is called "blood clot", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone embedded in the flesh, it is called "fistula"; and if the leather is that you can grasp that leather all around, and even when it is subtle, as a draped veil; and it does not move from its corruption.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the limb is fractured, if it does not leave the wound closed; if you do not cover the wound edges as you see, if it appears in this manner, that the limb bends lower than it is, for when the limb is fractured, if it does not leave the wound closed and you do not cover the wound edges as you see, if it appears in this part: that the limb bends slightly forward, and does not leave anything of the limb; take solidifying medicines to put out the fracture, and extend over a drape of linen that covers the whole wound; then close the force where the break is most extensive, because there is often swelling upon the other drape according to the quantity of the break, and put it over the break of the limb to align the limb, and do not remove the great drape until after once; and that which is outside the break often supports the limb, and its flesh is what corrects the fracture, if that be from poison or wound or enough, or digestion or indigestion; take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine is in this part extended and you see the nature that jumps upon the break, if its flesh has already gone, and approach the health; then remove the fracture in the morning, or the third day, and when you remove the fracture, if it changes the other drape, renew the swelling.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if it is found to be dislocated again after being adjusted, the limb remains stiff and does not yield.</start_of_turn>
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	If subtle drops appear after a long tension, do not fear for your life, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If subtle drops appear after a long tension, do not fear for your life, for health is approaching. For there are some who delay their healing from their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if it be indigestive spurting from the belly after remaining still for a while, the veins that were previously closed open again; and if the veins take too long to recover, it swells and becomes loose, so that if you do not take medicine that is drying in essence and moist in virtue, as is often the case, there is much vitriol; and this is the last medicine. Take diaphinit and make it with rose oil and the root of elderberry, equal in substance; then confirm and use it. The same thing makes excellent ointment for engrosed wounds, when diaphinit is not present, or take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them up, and sprinkle them on the honey when it is taken off the fire; then add a bandage and remove it from the belly, and do not give an antidote for a long time, or angelica root and celestial thistle, which is like fine flour and poppyseed; and use them in simple or compound form: grind them up, make powder of them, and sprinkle them on the honey that I have mentioned above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess incision.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that originates from the swelling of the pouch of the hand, or the foot, or sometimes occurs in other places; and when it is envious, and one does not take care, if it comes there will be an abscess that bursts and ruptures the root of the swelling, and sometimes bursts all the way through; and there comes the corrosion until the bone, so that there is severe pain, and the head of the bone is loosened, and the colour is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you have cured it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, if you must, take away all the superfluous parts that are remaining from the swelling, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is great help if the bone is sound, and the swelling is painless; but if the swelling presses on the marrow and begins to swell, and the marrow bursts, if you must put all the marrow out of the swelling as much as possible, and leave only the outer part; then apply medicines that are arden and corrosive to the bone until all is removed. Then cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the bone is corroded, if the head of the bone breaks and thrusts forward, for as much as the corrupted bone is, it cannot be healed; and if you see the bone breaking in two, if the head of the bone is in front as it should be, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is raw, bleeding, and causes great pain, it is certain that you must heal it first; then break the bone through the spur of the scapula, and guard that the cut does not reach the cartilage which is below the spur, for the patient would feel too great pain; and if it happens, put something over which will soothe.

The two joints which arise in the hands of some men by chance are always fleshy, and in some there is bone, and never is there a nail, and never are any born in the root of the joint, or are they born in our hands from the two joints.

He who is born in no wound does not move; and he who is born at the joint of the wound, by chance moves; the size of him that is fleshy is slight, in part like a small spindle.

Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment for iron is in two ways: one is with the cupped hands, and treat with the black bile; and the other way is to ligate the vein, and treat all with force.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first raise the affected limb high and warm, until the swelling is reduced; then strain the limb of the patient from under the hip joint up to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one, two or three places, of a large size; then ligate and pull out the black bile from your hand, from one armpit to the other, until as much as the patient can endure; and then ligate and command him to eat flesh without black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, without harming the patient.</start_of_turn

The nourishment of this kind is as follows: open the limb of the patient, if there is much hair, then put or bathe it in warm water, and raise the limb high until it turns red, and swell the veins; and if you do not have water, if the fire is applied, and then press the skin over the long part of the elbow, or in the part below the ankle; then ligate the skin to the bone, and loosen the vein from the heel part, until it appears when it is felt; and you will see it red and black, and when it enters or the skin seems as if like a white thread; then draw out the bone until it is freed from the skin, then put on the ligature lightly, and press in another place nearby; then press again of a larger size, or several if you must, and leave it, and press at the nail, then draw and leave just until the second size; then draw out size for size until it is all out, and leave it; and if you do not draw it out and lift it, if there is a nail at all the end of the thread, bind and draw it, and there will be blood at the nail, and twist your hand from one side and the other, until it is gone; and keep that it does not swell, for if it swells, it will not be possible to draw or lift it, and will cause harm to the patient; and when you have finished treating it, take out the bone from the wound and cover it with coarse cloth and oil of roses.

de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.

This vein is contained in the limb, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it arises elsewhere except in the limb, and this comes from the decay that comes from the outer skin towards the inner parts, as in the case of the serpent’s body and towards, containing between skin and flesh
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante. If the limb is opened, if it is thought that a piece of sponge should be wrapped around one and a half inches up to two and a half inches, and the knot, and let the sponge rest in the limb, and every time that it has come loose, if the wrapping is around the sponge, and the knot, and if it is too long, if you cut off a part, and wrap around the rest, do not cover the root; for if you cover it, it returns into the flesh and causes swelling and inflammation or bruising, and makes the disease worse; therefore it is necessary that it be treated immediately and without delay until it is completely expelled, without leaving anything or residue; and in no way must this vein be treated with more than five fingers or ten, and one hon has already come to me from ten fingers, from which it was expelled. des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow, or at the wrist, and there comes moisture from the rupture; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease", because it often causes the patient to vomit; it is a small vein that arises between skin and flesh, and runs throughout the body, ascending and descending, and is felt all over the limbs, as long as the skin is stretched or pulled, and sometimes bursts; and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as blood, worms, and bile or belly-ache; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it runs through the body and reaches the head, it sometimes returns and destroys the marrow.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not go away, then do this: bind the limb above and below with a strong thread, then put a cautery on the surface and burn it until it dies; for the greatest harm that it does is when it runs counter to the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, strain from it the hair that grows on the edge, then put a cautery on, and burn it. And use the patient of purgatives of corrosive medicines for the bad humors that are carried, and give him nourishing food.

This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs, and as it moves from limb to limb; and I saw that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and found her with her arms swollen, and saw a small swelling in the belly of the arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise up like a worm on the shoulder, more swollen than anything, as if there was silver under the skin that burst out of its place, and went into the shoulder, and then afterwards corrected itself throughout the limb, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it would turn back towards the limb as often as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it twisted back inwards towards the body, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I do not wish to say that it is because of great pain that she does not want to move from limb to limb, but I do not believe her; for I saw the same thing in the woman; and I thought that it was because her bones were dry and her veins were exposed, and because of that appeared that constraint; and I do not understand it according to these things that are delicious, and which have moist bones and veins restored

And when you see the healing of this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if the swelling above and below has persisted, and then press over until the wind pressure is overcome; and cauterize the limb. des saiettes	And when you see the healing of this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if the swelling above and below has persisted, and then press over until the wind pressure is overcome; and cauterize the limb. And if you do not see it in your eyes, if he is cured of that which causes the wind pressure, as foul pills, and pilules of serpin, and similar things.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The towels are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they relieve.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that some have large points, some have small, some have teeth, and some have bristles; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and the one that breaks in no limb breaks in two ways: either in the principal limb, as the brain, the shoulder, the liver, the spleen, the intestines, the bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the limb is dislocated in any part of the body, and the sign of death is present, as I shall tell you later, you will learn: if you delay the extraction of this arrow, for death will follow in many dispositions; and when this is a bad sign, do not delay any longer, for the arrow is not entirely withdrawn, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the limb is dislocated and the arrow pierces the bone, and the blood spurts from the wound which is above the brain, this is when scraping and soiling and vomiting and fainting and redness of the eyes, swelling and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes without vomiting, or without hearing, or without speech; and sometimes the speech is lost and the voice is stifled; and spurting of white moist blood resembling pus, and also as blood-stained urine; and if this sign is present, if you delay the cure, extract the arrow if it is not already withdrawn.</start_of_turn>
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When the wrist strikes or breaks, the signs are that it is near the left breastbone, and feels as though it were fixed in something hard, not soft; and by chance the wrist moves like a poulp, with dark blood, and brings cold sweat and cold chills, and fainting: it signifies great doubt that death is imminent.

And I pulled out an arrow from the king’s prince who was lying in the middle of the night; and his face was pale on the right side; the arrow was completely recovered. I went to the cure after it had been lying for three days
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very inflamed.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I would make it at all a gentle attempt, and I would not feel it myself; and there would be no pricking or pain at the edge of it.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of an arrow. I put on a protective dressing that would digest the infection, so that it would not swell; and I saw the blood appear from the wound
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I held the dressing firmly in place, and closed the wound, and left the patient lying down for a long time, until he felt the arrow was gone from his flesh; and he confirmed it to me
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on an aggressive corrosive medicine on the wound for a long time, until it was burnt out, and I held it, and felt the tip of the arrow coming out of the flesh; then I closed the wound with this medicine, until the tip of the arrow became visible; and it went well until the end of the chapter, as I have shown, until I took out the stitches, and I brought the wound together from one side and the other, and I could not do anything; so I had to continue to undermine and torment in many ways, until I finally took out the stitches, as it is shown at the end of this chapter, as I have described, until I took out the stitches, and restored the wound
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it therefore, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or as you said concerning the quality of the extraction of some arrows, if you put your cure on that which I do not wish to tell you, for the books do not teach me; but you masters know well enough concerning many great things, and concerning that which is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, descending from the things that happen in this art.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not issue from members or are sewn falsely, for it is not in two ways: either by the loop or that they enter; or by any other way. And that which leaps forth by the heel or enters, is an arrow transfixed in the flesh, and leaps never again at this moment.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not happen now, let it stay until the chariot is fully borne, and rejoice at its issue; and if it is fixed in the bone and cannot be dislodged, even if you leave it for some days, and move it little by little; then it will happen. And if it does not happen, pierce through the entrails until the wheels are expanded, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the splinter is fixed in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the things that I have said above concerning the patient: if you do not treat it, but leave it as it is until it is even again after some days, for if the splinter reaches the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the splinter is fixed only in the bone and does not reach the surface, and remains in the patient for some days without any other accident, if the limb is not treated properly.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the moisture-soaked flesh is fixed and will not yield, if you administer tarres around it as I have told you; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the splinter is embedded deep within the flesh, if it cannot be seen, if the pain is severe; if you feel it, if there is no obvious instrument to grasp it; if you cannot grasp it by the wound edge or by the depth of the splinter, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the pain is great; grasp the splinter firmly and if there is an earring caught in the flesh at the point where you grasp, if the ear is caught by the bone of the two parts of the jaw that you grasp, and then break or pluck out the earring of the splinter as much as you can; and do so cautiously so as not to break the splinter, but rather to grasp it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not succeed at once, if the limb remains bent over, then grasp it firmly, for the extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the evacuation of blood contradicts the treatment in this chapter; mix with what we have said concerning the cure. Beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put in something like that which you will use to grasp the splinter without peril, or twisted or taut, or firmly or gently; and set the patient as he was when the splinter was embedded, for that is the greatest aid of all, and if you cannot do this, do as the signs show you
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The wound comes from elsewhere, or it is open without any mark, or the skin is swollen in the place where it is seen or felt: in such a case, hold the edges together until the teeth can take hold, and then remove it: if it happens now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it does not withdraw, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; if there is any remaining arrow, if it is full, remove it entirely; if it is chipped, and you see that it has become loose, apply pressure immediately, if you apply an instrument with a hook, so that the tip of the arrow is caught in the hook of the instrument; and then pull out, and if the arrow is caught, pull out the instrument with the tip entering the wound, to lighten the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, then you must take hold of all the surrounding flesh or the venom is there, if you believe so; then cure the wound as it seems right.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the wound is near the bone, flesh, belly, bladder, or ribs, and is close, and you believe it is touching, then hold over the area that seems to be touching; and protect the belly and nerves, then extract the foreign body, and then close the wound, if necessary; and cure as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which we treat the splinters is similar to the beak of an eel, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the tip of the bone is like the quill of a bird, to push out the point of the wound, as in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the nails to push and to grasp if it is like this:</start_of_turn
des voinnes dou cors communes	From common veins.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins of which we know of more or less sixteen in number: two veins that are behind the ears, which are above the bones; and two arteries that are in the two temples that appear; and two veins that are in the two armpits, which are called "aspire"; and the vein that is under the nose; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and two veins that are at the collarbone; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins of the arm are five in number: one is the cephalic, which is on the left side of the elbow and is called the superficial vein; the second is the median, which is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins and is called the deep vein; and the third is the basilic, which is either on the front or back of the elbow and is called the radial vein, and is above the ulnar bone.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The ulnar vein is between the olecranon and the ring finger, and if there are two of them; and in the leg and the thigh there are three veins: one which is below the cubital vein on the inner side of the elbow, and the second which is behind the ankle on the outer side; and the vein which is called the sural, which is in the ankle of the other leg; and in the other leg there are three veins like these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of veins that are behind the ears is of great help for old purges and for emigration; and their qualities of health, as I have said, is that you raise the head of the patient, and wipe the hand or the veins are of a rough texture; then stretch the patient's neck with a pin, until the two veins behind the ears depend from the head: if the patient has a throbbing pain in his head, or feels a swelling of the face, this is a sign of infection; then take the lancet, and prick the vein until it reaches the bone, then keep your hand over the whole vein upwards, and press and squeeze the skin and the vein well two must pass through, and make the bleeding cease as soon as you see; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmie accustomed, and at the root of tears of water there are drops; and the quality of the physician is such as I say: and that the patient strains his neck, as the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse down his forearm, then he marks it; then he takes hold of the thumb on his forearm at the index finger, and pulls out the lancet down, and the vein up, and the clot, as he has done in two other veins, and makes cure of the blood according to his necessity; then he frees the patient, and puts his forearm on the vein for an hour, then puts on a bandage; and then the swelling forms, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of it above and of its evacuation, or of its beginning in the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood of the front vein is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein; it has diseases of the old face, embolism, and redness; and the quality is that if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as the vein opens; then take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood of the front vein is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein; it has diseases of the old face, embolism, and redness; and the quality is that if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as the vein opens; then take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this. Place the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow as much as you see fit; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never leave it with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not permitted for me to say that the flame should be too thick; and the same with the vessel, for the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.</start_of_turn
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are two finger-widths wide helps with the swelling, and the tension, and the redness, and the yellowing of the oil; it has diseases of the face. The quality is that if the patient strains his neck by twisting from side to side, as before; then do the same, and either let the blood flow freely, or for a long time with a wide flame, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make pressure of blood as much as you can manage, and then bind above and below, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	When the blood of the vein does not flow as it should, if it is for an age-related weakening, or for sickness of the face, such as measles and redness that appears on the face, and even when it is old; and if the quality of the blood is that the patient stretches his neck, then strain his jaw to your left hand, take a long flame and hold it over the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well enough at this point, and do not proceed until you have corrected it; do not go too quickly, and correct the blood according to your need, then leave it for a night, for it is too dry to restore. This is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two veins helps to loosen the swelling, and to commence mixing, and to relieve many diseases, and to remove boils, and corruptions, and herpes, and stones; and the quality of the blood is that the patient stretches his neck both front and back, as we have said; and either the master is standing above the patient’s head, and the patient sits on one seat, then open the vein widely, and draw blood steadily, or as much as is necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then remove the ligature, and strain both middle veins gently, that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the livers.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms above helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the arms, and toothache and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And you shall take hold of the patient’s head and turn the liver, and behold both veins, one of which is to the right of the liver and the other to the left, and you shall know them by their blackness, and by that which runs into them small black veins: thus take one and the other, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, if you take the greater one from the front, and thus also the two lower ones, for this is a like manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And of the blood of the veins the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the cephalic blood, and this is at the expansion of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and you hold the tongue, and look under each rib towards a black vein: take both of them, but do not go too deep, for under them are the arteries
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins which are commonly cauterized are usually sound in two ways: either by pricking with a sharp flame of moderate size, or by means of an olive oil cautery as with incised trenches; and it is called ‘anesil’; and they are large and subtle according to the size and extent of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of the fire cautery is known to be round, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there must be a cautery master who, when opening the large veins filled with visible blood and containing much blood and trouble, employs the olive oil cautery form
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for healthier veins, or there is citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps to cause diseases such as sore throat, and cough, and pain in the belly; and it is necessary that it flow steadily, and that it cease from the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If he grasps the limb, and blood flows from a wound, if it is deemed necessary, I say; do not hold back the flame, but cut as if for an animal.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the vein does not open visibly, if you must extract it, and bind another; or you wish no blood to flow, or you wish to keep the vein closed in the arm: it will open visibly; and grasp the flame firmly, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see that the blood vessel is dislocated, if you must therefore extract the limb, touch the limb until you know its position; then mark the limb, and then bind the limb, grasp the vein with the flame firmly; and beware not to wound the artery when you see the limb swell, for that is the artery: stop it immediately
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it swell up high like the urine of a child, and it is without redness or swelling, know that it is without an artery: haste then, and put your thumb on its length, and press your thumb until it stops bleeding; for often it happens; if you loosen your hand, leave it alone, and do not move the patient; and be cautious, and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not stained, and it swells, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts, because the head of the humerus is retracted; hold it still without.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a pinch of alum, and press it in, and take half of it and put it on well until the other half; if it stops bleeding, that is good; if not, if the physician has said, powders that stop bleeding; and the bleeding must not be great in many situations because of the little size of the wound, and the power of the hand
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps to cure blood clots at the root of the head and the armpit, for it is composed of the basilar and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is useful for the patient to be aware of the nerve that is below, and if it is not too deeply embedded, and if he can find the nerve, he will swell it and the blood will either clot or recover; and by chance it cannot recover. This nerve is often opened many times, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, it is necessary to take the blood from the anaesthetic instrument and abandon the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if the vein is long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein helps to cure blood clots at the root of the head and the armpit; it aids in evacuation of the clots. It is useful to cauterize with the olive or mirtin flame, for this is the most effective of all veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Whatever be the case, it is best to ask for the lightest blow the first time, and grieve nothing if it does not take hold; and by chance it may take in a few homes, which cannot be forced the first time, but grieve nothing.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know of health is that blood should only be drawn when necessary to preserve health and to ward off future diseases; and it should be taken from one of the three veins that are or should be open: that is to say, the cephalic, facial, or brachial; and it should be done at the commencement of prayer before meals, and during sleep afterwards when hunger has passed when the sign of repletion appears; and it should be drawn the first time or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood which is drawn for diseases has no fixed dose, but should be taken when necessary in the morning or evening at any time; and it should not be drawn from children until they are twelve years old, nor from women for more than four months up to seven times
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Must not be given to those who have passed 60 years.</start_of_turn>
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When anyone appears to be well, in whatever way, if it be known that he has swallowed a lighter object, if there be teeth retained in his mouth, so that the veins do not draw out intestines by force, neither from too much meat nor from its being raw or spoiled; and if he vomits after eating, and has a swollen belly, and multiple pains, and a loss of appetite, and excessive sleeping, and sadness, and such things as are caused either by the weapon or by poison; then subtilize the humors, if they are not large, by means of food, drink, and medicine, if you can. Then let him either bathe or drink, without anything hindering, to subtilize the blood, and keep him warm for a third part, as we have said. Keep him employed, attentive, and merry, and join his hands and feet together. Let him be raised up more than usual, and lightly stroke his arms two or three times, then draw out the thread from below the middle, because if it is too taut or loose, it cannot be corrected without. Then stroke the limb with your hands, until the veins swell up and are felt. Then moisten the patient’s face with a little oil, then put his left hand on the vein below the elbow, and hold it for a moment or two until he appears to be well, that the vein does not burst and cause injury.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run as swiftly as strings to the hanger, and if some of them are filled with wind, so that when one puts the flame on, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, then one is in this case. And if one opens the vein, the wound is too wide, for this reason one must advise the hanger in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good; if not, it must be repeated again either immediately or later, for if the patient is not relieved.</start_of_turn
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is inflamed and the patient hopes that it will heal by itself, leaving it for a year or two, and does not bind the arm: by chance there will be abscesses in the flesh; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops; and if the wound is small, or if it is not properly treated and you doubt whether there will be as much blood as you see, even if you apply the flame directly; and do the work carefully, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb inflamed, do not recommenmence the bleeding, but place above it a little pot of oil of castor, for it softens the flesh of blood; and it is muedre in this limb the oil that is in it; and give the oil of castor in small amounts so that you stain the veins, to stop the course of blood; and this very thing makes the swelling subside and the pain diminish, when it is placed on the limb; if it is subtle and does not escape when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, even if it is not dangerous except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, if you are hasty, and put on the limb a wet sponge and a little pot of salt, and strain for an hour; and believe that you have done enough after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in the limb after a few days no blackness or greenness, if it does not bother me; and if you see that, do not put anything else on it of aloes or myrrh, but keep it scraped with vinegar, mustard, or something similar.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is abscess and appearance at the root of the nail: put your hand there, and if you feel the root soft under the pressure of your hand, if it is that kind of appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave off any article that is not essential to the meaning of the sentence.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And take out each piece of blood according to the amount of its virtue, and its color.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is dark without, if you leave it until it is red; and if you see it big, if you leave it until it is slight; and if it is too thick, if you let it cool down.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is to be known to him who is plain and strong, and has need of extracting blood, that we must make the wound larger; and let the flame be great. And to him who is feeble, do the contrary, and make it safer and more frequent, and must do so by cutting across, not by pricking; for this method of bleeding is safe from the decay of blood and nerves, and is worth more than blood that flows long rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him who has cold blood, it is to be given soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is pale, let him take blood three or four times. And if he is of pale complexion, let him mix in front of the blood soft bread soaked in honey, or in aromatic honey with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and sweet-smelling honey.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he drinks at the blood, after the issue of mouth blood, it is to be believed that he will vomit bile, an odorous liquid, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the belly.
