de la routure de la mandibule	Of the route of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without injury to the surrounding tissues, and the fracture is slight, and not deeply fractured, except for the teeth which must be loosened gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is appropriate, if the fracture is in the distal part, to bite down on the index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take the index finger of the right hand, and touch the fracture gently, and hold it steady with the other hand in turn, and make it equal
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if it is recommended that you administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth arises, or swelling, if strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a broken jaw cerote on the jaw and put on a double drape; and on the drape place a large well-made patty, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and bind it to the tooth that you wish, and command the patient to rest, and feed on soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, if it comes loose at the root, and then return to its place; put on a plaster on it, with coarse powder of almonds with abundant eggs or oatmeal, after you have set the cerote; and put on a soft bandage, and if the plaster comes loose, and the patient’s condition does not change, leave it as it is until it heals; many times it heals in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a wound comes out, if it threatens what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, heal so that no part of the bone is left bony; if subtle of the bone has instruments covering it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, if it has flared up as you need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have sutured all these pieces, and there is no more bleeding, if the wound is wide, and put on some covering materials that cover the wound, to absorb moisture, until it is healed
de la forcele	and strong.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and if it breaks in two ways: either it is broken and loosened in three parts, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	When the break is in line with the wound, have two assistants; one should hold the limb that feels the force of the break; and the other should extend the neck towards the part; then put the break back in place so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither bulge nor swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend it further, put under the patient’s shoulder a round ball of lead, or cloth, as thick as you need; and extend and keep the forcele, and strain the lead at your hand, so that you can put the break back in place as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you are unable to manage the head of the shoulder when it comes out of its place, because it will slip downwards, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his heel, and put the shoulder in its place, that is, the middle ear, and hold the minister in the lower part of the shoulder until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris, know that you must cut there; and extract the fragments gently, and if the bone will not join together by any means, if the socket has been damaged at one of your incisors, but that you put in place the shoulder instrument to protect the face.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, but it is not crooked, and be as wide as it ought to be, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the curve of the wound that you made when you treated the bone; and when you are sure of the apposition, if the wound is slight, or if you doubt the apposition, if you use a dressing and a bandage, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the wound has become infected, if there is moisture, let draping with oil of roses, and balsam, and wine, and put on it.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stretching of the bone, when it is sensible to wounds and to the surgeon, is that you put upon the bone the plaster of the powdered mill and eggshell, and put on light bandages, and put a pin between the scapulae if necessary; then take a great bandage of a palm of a hand wide, then put on a double drape over the bandages, and plaster; then take a staple of three fingers wide and long, and wrap around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is pendant; and put the staple on the bulge, and turn the bandage on the collar, and take off the pin of the shoulder, and take off the painful shoulder; and rest the limb part, and when you see that the ligament holds the bulge steadily, and that you clearly see that the staple does not move from the bone break, if you reward every jerk, and if it is released; and make the patient rest on his back, and put under his armpit a little cushion under the shoulder, to lift up the arm; if you align the fracture by aligning the shoulder blade, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not unbind it unless there is some evil happening that does not come, until about twenty days; then repeat the plaster if you see that there is need for it, and strain and leave it on until it is restored; and it is restored in about eight days, and in less time for most people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then restart the dislocation, if you see that there is need for it, and hold and leave it alone until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time than most men.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the broken or dislocated shoulder, do not attempt to move it until it is set in its natural position; if it is displaced according to the break, reduce it following its natural form in all ways possible. Then pour the powder of wheat with eggshells, and apply light pressure, and place over a double bandage. Then place a broad and firm splint over the shoulder, which is wider than the shoulder itself, and ensure that the heel of the splint is firmly fixed in no part of the shoulder. If necessary, use a linen dressing to hold it firmly in place. Then tightly bind the shoulder with a strong bandage, ensuring that the splint does not move from its place. Observe the patient’s breathing and pulse; and whenever there is relief, if you loosen the bind and replace the splint if necessary, lay the patient on their side. The shoulder will be restored in twenty days or less. When this time has elapsed, if the fracture has healed, rejoice, for it is not bone that has been easily displaced.

And if a piece of the bone sticks forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone, do as we have said concerning the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone sticks forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone, do as we have said concerning the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The body is never completely broken in the middle, but this often happens thus; however, it often breaks upon sudden exertion.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in two, if it declines with pain, and feels great pain, and is pale, and vomiting blood, and the jaw is split open in the broken bone, and one feels very well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez. de la brisure des costes	And if the patient lies still on his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and subtly make them even in all positions until the limb is restored to its normal shape; then put on splints and bandage with fine salt or other soft material, and cover with a cloth, and bind firmly over the broken bone, if it does not move; and turn the limb around the back and strain it gently, and award some time the limb, and if it relaxes, strain it again; and if it comes loose again, because of corrosion or inflammation that comes from the bone, or pain or swelling, if you are hasty, loosen it and remove the splint, and address the cause of the fracture; then restore the splint and strain it until it is healed.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fracture of the bones only comes from great pains after the back, and at the head of the shoulder, and they do not happen for anything else except that they are slippery; and the patient often feels them at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is that you must put the fracture back in its place as it should be

And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inwards, if the patient feels great pain, and swelling, like with pleurasy, because the bone touches the gut; and there are pains, and vomiting, and vomiting of great quantity of blood, this is a grievous disease, and they have put great pain on it.</start_of_turn>

Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except in the case of ulcers that do not heal, when they have not appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have appeared, if they are healthy.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one puts a bandage on the limb because of its swelling; for this is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not draw out the excess moisture from the limb because of the weakness of its position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth soaked in oil, but put on bandages between the ribs to keep the wound even, then either cure with a pleurisin dressing, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the liver, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is possible to cut above the fractured bone, and if it is necessary, you must drill into the bone, and remove the splinter, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with bandages, until it is healed
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If after the incision the wound bleeds, put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb; cure while the limb remains in this position, without pressing on the costing bone or anything else, until the bleeding stops.
de la brisure dou col	If the rib is fractured,
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	The rib is often fractured along with the collarbone, and often blood flows; and the spine is also affected
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	When this is finished and you know if it is healed or not, if you see his hands softened and limp and dead, and that you cannot move or extend them, and if you prick them with a needle, if there is no sensation there
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The wound is mortal in many situations, and if you move them and feel well when you strain and prick them, the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient is cured, if you put on cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if something similar happens at the hip joint, and you know if it is healed or not, if you take care that the thigh bones are soft, and if there is an accident at the hands or on the back, with swelling and vomiting, without wanting to; and when you have soothed it on the belly, if there is swelling and vomiting without wanting to
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and sees the ass, if he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	When he is lying on his back and sees the ass, if he cannot labor in his cure (heal).
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, if the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that if there is an abscess, if you prick it with a needle, put on rose oil or oil of rue marigold, until it is calmed; then put on one of the soothing and drying patches, and bind it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if a bone breaks, if you must cover on the limb; and unite the fragments of the wound, if it is large, with a bandage, then cure with oil that fills the wound, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is fractured, which is called the «fracture of the marrow», if it is on the outside of your left hand, and put it equal to the other hand on your side, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you need them; then strain it, and if there are broken bones underneath, if you leave it there, and unite the bones, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	and the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, if there is no other injury to the head; and if so, it is long and hangs down, and causes the patient pain in the limb, swelling, and bending of that which is fractured.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	If the fracture is at the head of the thigh bone, extend your hand over the fracture as long as you are over the break; and hold the limb in such a way as to reduce the fracture and restore its natural position. If the fracture is only at the head, leave it in its natural position.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long or downward, make the patient lie on his belly, until the restoration of the fracture is complete.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set them even, if you place them on the shoulder, then put on a staff of wood or bone, and hold the brace still, so that it does not move; and use the weight of the limb to stretch the ribs, as long as the limb is flexible.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if swelling comes, if it does not subside, until the swelling subsides, put on what we have mentioned before; and then rest, and stretch if it is convenient, without any mishap; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And thus make two incisions on the shoulder, and draw out the bone upwards, and hold the patient above a seat; then gently bend the arm down towards the elbow, with a curve of the arm, then place something heavy on the fist, or the minister extends the arm backwards; then put the eyes level with the hand clasped, until the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is if you support the patient on his shoulder, and bind the arm to his collar, and order the attendants that one holds what is above the dislocation at his hands, and the other holds the shoulder bones apart, and stretch the skin outwards.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, if you strain I lift the spleen, on the spleen, and extend thumbs of the ministers at his side
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the spleen is close to the head of the shoulder, you must put I lift half of the shoulder away from the elbow, and the other towards the ribs, from the elbow; and if the spleen is towards the ribs, you must put I lift it lightly, with effort, as long as the spleen is even on the arm and the ribs; then put the spleen back in its place if it is possible, and hold it, because if it does not come back by itself.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the wound does not close, if it does not tighten by itself, put on moist linen and rose oil until the wound is calmed; then tighten, and the manner of tightening is that you put the support on the briseure, then assemble the limb on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; put the bandage, and tighten on the support and the limb, so that the limb is steady, without anything hindering it, or without moving the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, if you use pins, put on the briseure a pin that is wider and stronger than the others, and put between the thumbs of two pins as much space as the thickness of two pins; then tighten on the pins, as I have said above concerning the chapter on the briseure, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the swelling of the testicles and the tightening, as we have said, in the area where you restore the limb, and you doubt the completeness of the cautery, if you leave it until the seventh day, as we have said; then look for three days afterwards, that the swelling does not increase or that new swellings do not appear in the limb, or that the swelling does not return to the limb for the reason that it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the swelling persists, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such thing happens, if not more than three days have passed, and the patient lies down on his back and has his hands on his stomach; and put a cushion under the limb one inch thick and even, and watch for an hour or two, that the limb is not stiff or that the ligaments are not slack; if the swelling subsides by the power of medicine, and do the meat that we have before you, in part as much as the meat is at the first tension; and when it starts to recover, even if it is somewhat large
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and limb must be restored in forty days of all; and then one must loosen them and administer poultices and medicines of ointment to the limb for the better.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is painful and embolded, it must be loosened in two days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	... of the breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". The former is small and is that which supports the pouch [of muscle]; the latter is large and is that which is bowed, towards the little finger. By chance the large radius alone breaks, or the small, and by chance both together break.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the little bones are fractured, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the great bone is fractured, if the healing is bad, and more painful than when they are fractured whole
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When only the little bone is fractured, if the limb is slightly extended, and set equal
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if the great bone is fractured, if the limb must be more strongly bound; and stretch over I cushion, and keep the wrist of the hand higher than the other, and the little finger lower than the others, and let the patient cross his arms over himself, and I cushion in front of him higher than he, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then stretch the limb from the elbow to the wrist, or at I elbow, and another assistant at the other side
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then he puts the eye steady, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If it breaks into pieces, if you put some back into its place, and if there is none that prick at its root as before, you will not be able to restore it to its place, even if you leave it alone like we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If with the fracture there is a wound, as I have mentioned in the singular case; take the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	Then at the beginning of the restoration, blood clots sometimes emerge from the incision. If they are thick like felt, I cover them with rosin oil and white wax, so that neither is too thick nor too soft; and I cover them superficially, until the blood clots are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then I put on the cerate and I put in the support of fine flour with abundance of eggs, because I put in the stars, and let the star of the briseure be more firm, and a little wider than the others; and there must be six stars or more in a position: either that the briseure is in one of the bones, or in two; and is more strained above the briseure than elsewhere, and less every day as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the dressings be soft and moist on the briseure, and neither too hard nor too soft; and let the thread, which is strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Et renaisse le membre et le lien après quelques jours.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And restore the limb and the tendon after a few days.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And start the movement again, and if the tendon is softened and the bone is loosened, and similar things, if the patient endures it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the swelling does not return to the limb, because it is too tight, then you must soften it, indeed, and leave it alone for a while, until the swelling goes down, and then restrain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said do not come to the patient, if not until day XX.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or when it is necessary, then he should keep his hands on his collar, and let his collar be even, and take care of movement and spitting, and sleep on his back; and drink whatever is necessary for the restoration of this fracture in XXX days or in fifty, and sometimes in XX days, according to the composition and temperament of the virtues
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	From the breaking of the hand
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	When the hand is broken or wet, if it is known that the patient will travel, let the patient sit comfortably facing forward; then put the hand on a wide bandage, and stretch the broken bones evenly; put the bones back in their place, as well as possible; put on the plaster and bandage, if necessary; and if there is a wound, put on a bandage according to the amount of bleeding; and be covered with one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	When the fracture is in the armpit towards the belly of the limb, make a loop of bandage, and order the patient to grasp their broken limb; then tighten with a long bandage, and put on a collar as wide as the limb, and tighten it as much as it is convenient.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the wrist, if you must know, put a splint above and one below in the palm, so that the thumb is over and straight, then bind it all around the wrist, and seal the loop between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to neither of us, if it is at the elbow, if you must know; put it even, if it is necessary; and strain it with the palm, and if you see that you must put a right-angle splint to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, if like in the index or one of the others, if you must put it even, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or you bind them all together, holding firmly, as much as is useful, or you put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in the restoration and in the arrangement of the burn, and cure what comes with it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	And if the break comes to neither of us, if it is at the elbow, if you must know; put it even, if it is necessary; and strain it with the palm, and if you see that you must put a right-angle splint to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, if like in the index or one of the others, if you must put it even, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or you bind them all together, holding firmly, as much as is useful, or you put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in the restoration and in the arrangement of the burn, and cure what comes with it, as I have said.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and one sees it when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound with a thread above the fracture and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, and extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is embedded in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the thigh bone, if either of the ligaments around the knee joint is ruptured, and the other is stretched by the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If also it is close to the knee, and then either the ligament from the knee joint and the one from the heel are ruptured; then put the bone in its natural position with two hands, until it is in its normal position, and then put on the dressing and bind it securely, for no other remedy comes.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess above, if you leave it calm and return to your work and your cure; the ligature is made in part for that.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with a strong bandage doubled twice in two or three places, and to drain the superfluous blood; then twist the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and pass a thread along the thigh from the knee downwards; then twist the limb and the thigh together with the strong bandage, and place the fracture in its place with two nails.  Then put three layers of bandage over the fracture; and the more layers you put on the fracture, the less the strain; then take out two threads that you passed through the thigh and knee, and put three nails underneath; then return to the nail head as before, until the pain has gone away; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, for no other remedy comes.</start_of_turn
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a loosening, if it comes loose, and if you address what has come; as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that prick, if it is necessary, it is to cauterize; if not, it is necessary to cut the vein, and drain away; and to cure as we have said, as long as it is necessary.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this case when it is set with sticks, as in the arm or the leg; however, in the restoration made in this case, I do not feel pain in the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And so, if the bone is reset in one day, or less or more, according to the diversity of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin street.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hair that is in the groin has often burst, but it falls many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If it breaks, if not a mere split or opening, and if there is pain, wound or sensation of pain, this is very well indeed.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the restoration is done, if you put everything round back in its place, as long as it is put together firmly, put the bandage on, and put on a round cushion, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the instructions that we have said before, as in incision and other things; if you put into each accident what it should be put in, as long as it is sound.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if the restoration is done, if you put everything round back in its place, as long as it is put together firmly, put the bandage on, and put on a round cushion, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the instructions that we have said before, as in incision and other things; if you put into each accident what it should be put in, as long as it is sound. And finish the fracture of the limb.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hair that is in the thigh has two bones, of which one is called the “muscle” and the other is called the “fleshy part”; and they often break together as much as the arm does, and for this reason the restoration is just as it is for the arm, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, if the limb is twisted in all parts
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured in two, the limb is twisted from the front.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	If the big bone is broken, there is great pain, and it is seen well; and it is twisted from its place.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	When thus the limb is brought into extension, and is set straight, and the bones are bound equally; nevertheless, if there is a break, it is of little use, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less violent and lighter; and the limb should be adjusted according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take four strips of coarse gauze that will cover the limb from one end to the other, and bind them around the limb from the knee to the toes; then cover with four layers of bandage, and bind firmly in the middle, and do not allow the limb to bend to the right or to the left, and it is well done; and no one should administer anything that is long along the limb, and if there is swelling, and it is of many pieces, that the extension should be less severe and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of bone fractures which are painful.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but in the bones of the limb there is no fracture at all, and two must suffice; and there is no other reason except for fear of death.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the limb, and you see these bones pressing against one another, if you put the limb so that it hangs in the air, as if it were flying away, and then put your limb back on the ground, where the bones were lifted up, then press on them until they return to their place; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put on a small bandage to the belly of the limb, then bind the limb steadily, and when you have bound it up, cover it with a cloth, and other things as you deem necessary
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if you loosen the dressing, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are fractured or displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there be two fractures, if you restore them as we have said, do so with two hands; then set a splint according to the length of the two bones, and make it wider than the former; then put on the dressing that I have mentioned. If there are three or more fractures, break them; and set upon each bone a splint according to its quantity, covered with a layer of linen, and strain the dressing down onto the bones.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have mentioned concerning other fractures, as we have said; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the thumb bone.</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the natural bone of a woman is fractured, if you make her sit expanded, then lean her forward towards the painful side; then fill the belly of the patient with cotton, and put as much as I stand; then drain the woman, and keep her back and front stretched out; and thus pull out the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and bring back the bone with the stone; and when she sees blood, if the stone is grasped by the cotton, and when she has bled, she will recover; and if the fracture is restored, if you see her, take a bladder of elderberry, and tie it to the part with a bandage, and bind up the bladder in the wound; then blow into the bandage until the bladder is expelled: the wound will then return the fracture; then fill with cotton and leave it as long as it is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or a woman is broken, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; these fractures which have proceeded from this study and practice will not be hidden from him who has undertaken it and has read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For these fractures signify in many ways the right way of restoration: indeed they must be known.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the limb, when it is broken, take a gooseberry and put it in the limb; then cover it with cloth, and leave it for two days or until it is healed, and it will be healed completely.
de brisure avec plaie	From the break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, as if it were the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it be set now, as the pain that we have mentioned testifies.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is well healed, if there is only a stain of vitriol, if you have nothing else, then resume the fracture in this way, or in that way, as soon as possible, for if there is no further displacement, the fracture will heal on its own.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there is displacement of the bone, if you leave the fracture undisturbed until the swelling subsides, as long as the displacement is not too great, and do not touch the bone or the surrounding tissue, for you will risk causing further damage.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks are apparent on the surface like a discovered wound, then you must know that you must press them lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the swelling does not appear to be pressing equally with your hands, if there is this instrument of iron which is about thirteen or fourteen inches long, and the breadth is according to the quantity of the wound; for this reason it must be applied with three or four fingers, as much as is necessary in the case of a wound of breaking. And let it be round and thick, so that it does not press too much on the limb during your work, and let it be before and thick in front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche" because it must be known that the curved bones must be placed over the head of the visible bone; and the latter must once again be restored, so that each may meet the other in an equal position
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, if you must copy the head of the bone as long as the instruments have possession of it
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you grasp with a covered instrument that can reach the area, or if you pierce or draw out, from that point forward remove whatever is remaining embedded in the bone, rough or soft scraps.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is likely that the marrow is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then moisten it with black vinegar and keep it covered; do not put any cerote or other thing on the wound, or there will be rancidity and corruption; then administer stars when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the surrounding area appropriately, according to the extent of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; for many times this has led to madness among fools, and has caused the patient to die or become paralyzed, or caused some other serious condition.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that there is no danger of further injury, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, if it is not possible to put on stars; but wrap around the limb, instead of stars, a firm bandage, and bind it firmly.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after one or two days that the wound is swelling, if the bone that you put on top has remained there for a long time, and if you put on healing dressings, like with tetracycline and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be immobilized in part as much as is possible so that it does not bend excessively easily.</start_of_turn>
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the limb persists in its displacement, and it cannot be reduced but returns to its place spontaneously, with small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you reduce the wound with care, and pull out all these broken pieces that cause this pain.</start_of_turn
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If a fistula arises in the body, or any other kind of corruption, if you must cure it, according to what is written in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	When the bone is fractured, and is opened on the limb, like the bones of the thigh or the shoulder, and other bones of the great limbs, if you do not treat it, for many people die from it; leave it alone until it has healed naturally; by chance it will mend itself after twenty days or thirty, and then cure the wound if you wish; if you do not wish, leave it alone
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From the beard which comes out from the beard hair.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	From the beard which comes out from the beard hair. Many times after the heat of the wind comes out of the joint, even when it is close to the limb; and it is a helpful sign to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot do its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that I am warned: if it has been administered stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollum, acacia, and similar things, that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that is stiptic or with abundance of egg or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain it well, and do not move it from hand to hand until it is healed; and then dislocate it, and do it again, until the dislocations are bony; or you strain it on a well-made piece of sponge; for the property of sponge is that it solidifies all the swellings under the limb; and if the dislocation has already turned into hardness just like stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above has burst, and to make the apparent excess; or you leave it without a drain, as long as it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone is restored, and hangs limp and limp after the limb is weak and limp, if there is any cause for it: because it was too tight and did not stretch enough; or because there are too many bands, and they do not permit the limb to move smoothly; or because of excessive bruising; or from too great a movement, not even in its hour; or because there is much blood in the flesh, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient walk, and tighten the limb, until it is strengthened in him; and give him baths, and make him merry and cheerful; then put on a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great nourishment, and the blood often turns red, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and then restore it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the disease.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, all in vain does it retain its natural movement: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have had this done in our land; this practice is blamed, and there results great harm, and by chance the death of the patient. However, if the swelling and torture are fresh, if you can raise them with warm water, or soften them with herbs such as elderberry leaves, root, and melilot, and similar things; and you do make an emollient plaster, as with aquilon well made, and take the nourishment of elderberry, and confit with butter of gelline or olive oil, and make plaster upon; or you take fatty figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that alleviate the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone loosened by continuous rubbing and length of time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And provide movement to the limb at the shoulder hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron tongs, if you cover it just to the bone, make a slight incision; and put cushions and padding in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no more, if you can now restore its normal position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if the limb swells up, and by chance if it is reset, there are pains at the root; for this reason it must not be moved while it is swollen: many times it brings swelling and other pains; however, when this happens, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him, until the swelling subsides; then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and support it lightly, and cure each limb as it comes to its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint to the end of the foot.
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	When the jaws are clenched, there are two common dislocations: either they are displaced from their sockets and softened by the muscle; or they are entirely displaced and hang downwards, causing the tongue to hang out of the mouth, unable to close the mouth and swallowing becomes difficult.</start_of_turn>
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will often spontaneously reduce on its own.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, if you must support it firmly, and do not be afraid; and in such a manner that the attendant grasps the head of the patient, and behold his pocket from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two must be defaced, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them all around
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And his eye should be level, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if the two jaws are together, if they arise with hot water and oil, so that they remain lightly; do not force to return it, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are restored equally, and the patient’s mouth is closed comfortably, if you put on moist cloths in a circle made of rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with thread; and let the patient rest on his back, and his arms be still between two cushions, so that they do not move neither to the right nor to the left, neither to the front nor to the back, but take a little meat, until the pains are gone; and then gently eat what you see lightly, and do not open your mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well numbed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws do not manage to be returned to their point at an hour, and are not otherwise converted at their leisure, if thereby fever and customary sickness arise, and by chance solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot remove from the bone without causing damage, and is useless every time it is attempted, and one can well tell.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies lying on his back, extends his arms; and then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then put on the bandage and bind it, and strain it; and the limb which is under the ribcage cannot be loosened; if not, and if it is loosened once, if you reset it in its place, as we have said; then put on the bandage and bind it, and strain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus will the shoulder be brought back to its place when it is relieved from its displacement.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The nails of the shoulder are loosened only in three ways: first, that they loosen from the heel to the toe; second, from the heel to the thumb; and by chance from the root to the tip, which is usual; do not loosen them from behind the shoulder, neither from below nor from above; and often loosen them from the toe towards the heel, even among those who have much hair, for at these leaps they are violently sick; among those who have enough hair, they leap with pain and return with pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens that there is a fracture or dislocation, and it inflates the shoulder with a hot abscess, and care must be taken that it is not displaced by this.</start_of_turn
