Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is appropriate to translate the text line-by-line:
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation is when it is pulled towards the heel, and it distinguishes between the sick and healthy shoulder, and you will find between their difference their displacement; and at the head of the shoulder you will find a pit, and from the heel to the shoulder touches the head of the shoulder, as if it were a wound; and the patient cannot move his hand back to its place, nor can he make any movement; and also, if it has been loosened high, if it is not hidden, for you will find it manifested by touching; and this manner of dislocation is not sufficient to bring back, when it is new, or when the patient is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician holds the painful limb upwards, then places his thumbs under the armpit, and holds the joint forcefully upwards towards the sky; and the physician holds the limb and extends it upwards, thus if necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as we have said before, if you must know, the patient must be immersed in warm water; and give him a soft and soothing emollient, such as a decoction of altea and fenugreek and melilot in water, or give it to him; then either lie the patient on his back and put under his seat a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, and put his elbow on the cushion, and keep his shoulder firmly in place, and treat the hand of the patient; and another minister holds the chief of the patient’s shoulder, so that it does not move forward; the shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it remains according to this method: and that you make present someone who is greater than the patient; and be two towards the cost of the shoulder, and hold the shoulder from the patient’s seat, and keep the seat high, so that the patient hangs down; and another minister treats the patient’s hand from behind the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, if he can carry nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And thus we can also do this: if the head of the shoulder is forced into the earth, where the arm is as round as a pillar and neither too thick nor too thin; then let the patient lie down with his shoulder draped in cloth, and let the arm hang down loosely; then extend the hand forward and the joint will return to its place immediately. And if it does not return by these things we have said, do this: take two fingers of two hands and three fingers wide, and put the thumb at the base of the little finger, as in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then he should lie upon the head of the shoulder draped with a cloth, so that the patient does not bleed; and put the hand of the patient behind the shoulder; and extend the arms above the shoulder, and place the shoulder against the arm, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm upon the shoulder blade of a broad shield, and extend the hands downwards, or leave the forearm hanging down from the other side: the dislocation is now corrected.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is corrected, in whatever way it is, if you command that you put behind the shoulder a ball of wool as long as it is even, then put on the shoulder pad with a sprinkle of wheat flour, with incense and alum on the whole shoulder and around, then strain out behind the shoulder immediately, and turn the limb on the shoulder pad, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is commanded that he should move little by little, until the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then move more after five or six days, and move it; and if it is firm and is not softened, if it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the joint is forced out of place by moisture or any other cause, then you must administer cautery three times over, as it is placed before or alongside the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and it loosens after three days, and the joint will not stay in place, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the elbow, and the bones, or behind, if it is made by impulse, and extension of the arms, and if another bandage is administered; and cure until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient with the limb, if he wishes to see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is tight, and cannot bend the arm, touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And it must be known that if it is possible to restore it again as before, when it has been pulled out, if it should grieve you to bring it back, for in such a case it cannot be restored altogether, even if it is at the furthest end; it is better that it remains dislocated than to be restored in this way, for it is of more great pain, and by chance it brings death.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and hold it from the root of the limb that is relaxed.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not see it return to its place, if you administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from the armpit, and when you have enveloped a double-long and wide bandage; and when you look at the joint with the hand, if there is any oil on the joint to soften it, then put on the joint, as long as it comes back; and when it is in its place, put on dry plaster with egg white, and the strain forms, and bend the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it for some days, then take it off.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, if you notice that it is not properly aligned, repeat the displacement and reinsert the limb, and leave it in that position for some days until it is firmly set; then you can remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, bathe and rub thoroughly, and press until it is eased; or put upon the joint a poultice of fat mutton grease, then leave it in place for a night, then remove the poultice, and wash; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the poultice, and then wash again; do this twice or thrice, until it is healed. If you see that it persists, put upon it a poultice of moist chaff with burr, and strain it off; if it returns to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand: the joint of the hand is loosened, and the return is laborious, more than any other joint in the body; it must be immediately repositioned in its place, while it is still loosened, even if the limb is swollen or if there is subsequent displacement.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you wish to reset the dislocation, put your hand gently on the patient’s shoulder, extend your arm, and look at the limb to ensure its placement; place the palm of your hand on the surface of the joint and press until it returns to its normal position. You must watch to ensure it is correctly aligned; then place your hand behind the limb on the shoulder at extension and flexion.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and I look put his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is well. If not, if the strain of the surrounding soft tissues has calmed, and you leave it in its place, it will recover naturally.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you do not put it back after a few days, the joint will become stiff; and it does no harm to the patient to leave it loose, and he can move nothing at all: except that if the nerves are cut or the arteries; if there is no other reason for straining except to cauterize, this is the only thing that is worth doing.</start_of_turn
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at rest, if you put on the bandage that we have mentioned, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no pain, if there is hot swelling, and you rub it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder of the arm</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never is the thumb detached from the wrist at the forepart, never at the back of the palm or belly; therefore let it go, and hold the dislocation at your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the thumb, and bend it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it for two days, and then set it straight; and do not touch it, as we have said, and withdraw the thumb, and move it, and bind it; and do this often, until it is well, and do the same if it is detached at the belly of the thumb, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is detached from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Due to the loosening of the scapula from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the scapula of the back or the neck is loosened, or if there are several loosenings, if there is no remedy, for the patient’s life is in jeopardy.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign that it is that the spasms of the urine flow in a contrary direction, it cannot be held back, and many times it softens no limb, or the two knees or the two arms or the face; and many times the spleen moves to three parts; that which moves behind is called "gilbosite": it is cured if the "gilbosite" comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres. I say that in the swelling which comes before the foot, there is no remedy; and also that which comes directly at the two costae, one cannot cure it except for that which comes from behind; as I have said; and that the patient’s face should be stretched out one inch even, and should be stretched from the toes up to the chest; then stretch the thumb at the wrist towards the earth and the other hand has a pincer grip, and grasp the patient’s ankles, and the other hand has haunches and knees, and ankles; and two ministers know the threads, one at the wrist and the other at the pincer grip, among the two thumbs; and let them be well closed, the thumb as we have said, and the patient should put his palms on the spine until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	If it does not return by this remedy, take a cube of three hands' length, and bind the part below the navel; let the patient lie on the side, and hold the head of the cube below the navel, then place the middle of the cube on the spine; put the thumbs of both hands on the other head of the cube, and press firmly until it returns to its place. If you see that it does not, do it at the wrist that swells at the hand.

If you see two veins at the head of the patient's arm of a great size, and two other pieces, and between each vein, a knot and a bandage of a palm's length; and in each vein a hole, or the wrist is corrected, and the veins are firmly bound, so that they do not move; and between each pair of veins there is one vein returning, so that the cord which is between the bones returns; and there are two small veins of a palm's length at the returns, in order to bring back the cord; and then join the cord which is between the bones to the cord at the head, and the other cord to the pieces at the other end, and bind the minister's cord to the whole length, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.

des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the shoulder.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Dislocations of the shoulder are only caused by dislocations of the shoulder and elbow joints; they do not occur with other joints. The dislocation of the shoulder is destabilized in three parts: front and back, and front and back; the more destabilized it is in front, the more destabilized it is behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And knowledge of dislocation is this: when you join the painful limb with the skin, if it is longer, and the patient groans more than usual, and cannot double his knee at the fire; and that is the bruise that is left inflamed by the cautery, for that is what causes the head of the humerus to come out of place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that he is well limbed as before; however, do not double his knee joint excessively with pain, and if you see him do so carelessly, do not attempt to stop him beforehand, and retain his urine, and swell his ankle, and when he walks, let him pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and is that his limb is shorter than the other, and his ankle is softened, and that his shoulder joint is dislocated at the root of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The head of the shoulder must be reset if an old dislocation persists, and it persists as before; and it is not to be presumed that any treatment will be effective.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are hasty in returning the joint, and stretching it inwards and outwards, and moving it to the right and left; by chance, if it returns, there is no need for any other treatment.

Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is often used in this case, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.

If this does not happen, if you must, provide care for its semblance. Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation. S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It is from wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound follows dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it has happened that the patient has died: if you are not cautious in the treatment, and if you do not know how to handle it and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and timely, do not be ashamed; and at the beginning use calming measures and support the patient’s head, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of recovery; and when you see hope, if you remember to reattach the limb now, even if the support remains; and when the limb is reattached, if you administer calming measures and treat the wound, as it should be, from dried ooze; and if with dislocation there is fracture, and bones are fractured, if the bones are displaced, do as we have said in simple illnesses; and beware of pride, as I have said, for this will bring you disgrace according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your arm and body.
